<Author>ksgirl8
<Content>Great Place to Stay in Heart of San Francisco We stayed here for a weekend in San Francisco. When we were there (fall 2008), quite a bit of rennovation was still going on in the lobby area so things like the restaurant and lounge were not totally available. However, despite that we really enjoyed our stay here. It seemed to be more of a place for business people. During the weekend we barely saw another person, but once Sunday night rolled around, it was crowded. We had a renovated room, which was stylish and comfortable. We had no complaints at all. Our view from the window was not good, but this didn't bother us. We were there during an unusually warm time and I felt the air conditioner could have worked better. It wasn't bad or unacceptable, but it was really the only non-stellar part of the stay. Since it was in the upper 80s, I doubt this would very often be any kind of issue. One great thing about the room besides the typical hotel amenities was that it had plenty of outlets so we could easily charge all our various electronics. The best thing about this hotel is the location. It is totally convenient to the trolley cars and also some bus lines. We didn't have a car at all except our last day and had no issues getting around. This hotel does have somewhat high fees. The wifi was somewhat expensive (maybe $12) and the parking was very expensive ($20+ a day) so I would keep that in mind, but we would definitely recommend this hotel to anyone desiring a comfortable and stylish base for their San Francisco trip.

<Author>Ricardodesantaalbana
<Content>Loved the Omni...well it was pretty good anyway I booked through a conference website for $160/night including tax. The location is good, near to Union Square, China Town and the Coit Tower and on a tram line. I was initially not impressed since everything seemed expensive (e.g. $6 bottle of water in the room - I used the tap). Also I didn't bother with breakfast at $20 for continental and $26 for cooked (perfectly good Chinese deli next door).You just need to join Select Guests and not only do you get free internet access (not Wi-fi yet though) but you are also treated to a free 2 morning drinks (e.g. posh tea and grapefruit juice) and a turndown service (which I'd never heard of): you come home to find relaxing music on and ice in the wine cooler and a chocolate mint!Any problems I had were dealt with well (free internet help line) and overall a positive experience. I don't usually like these rather souless posh city hotels, but this was pretty good after early reservations.

<Author>N4SLYF
<Content>Above  My partner and I stayed at the Omni San Francisco for 8 nights. I knew about this hotel from when I lived in San Francisco and worked in the Financial District. We booked an entire vacation on Hotwire and paid a little more to stay at the Omni only because I'd always wanted to stay there. Little did I know what an experience we were in for.We checked in on Saturday night. Crystal at the front desk immediately upgraded us to a concierge floor room. She was genuinely friendly, professional and outgoing. Check-in was quick and easy.The room was elegantly furnished. The only drawback was that it seemed small. We were there for eight nights and we found that it lacked storage for all of our clothes. I think for a shorter stay, the room would've been absolutely perfect. From the bellman to the front desk attendants to the valets to the doormen to the room service people, the service was nothing less than spectacular. Everyone remembered our names, what room we were in, had our car waiting for us in a timely manner. We had breakfast at Bob's Steak House one morning. The french toast is to die for and the portions are big. Though the food seemed expensive, the portion size made up for the price. The room was appointed with a plasma TV, king size bed with down comforter. We had turn down service nightly with water and fresh fruit waiting for us when we returned from the day out. We had drinks of our choice and newpapers waiting at our door every morning. The hotel was originally a bank that was gutted and rebuilt in early 2000's. It was beautiful on the inside and out. It didn't seem overcrowded at all. As a matter of fact, it seemed nearly empty most of the time we were there. It is located on California Street @ Montgomery, on the California Street Cable Car Line and in the heart of the Financial District. I liked this location because it was out of the way of all of the tourist traps and it was nice to come home at night to a quiet, much more relaxed environment. Though we are planning to move back to San Francisco in the coming year, I do believe that I will stay at the Omni again before we move and I will definitely, definitely suggest it to anyone coming for a visit.  
<Date>Dec 2, 2008

<Author>jsilverheart
<Content>I LOVE THE OMNI We stayed at the Omni over Labor Day weekend for 3 nights...I had stayed at this hotel before the year before in December, and fell in love with it... From the fresh fruit and refreshing lemonade in the lobby to the nightly chocolate on my pillow. Its all about the details for me and customer service.The Omni delivers. I love the fresh flowers in the lobby,the warm greeting from all staff members, the housekeeper's friendly notes, the rooms...I can go on and on...But I really love where The Omni SF is located. The financial district is bustling during the week, but on the weekends its quiet. The hotel is walking distance from the Ferry Building,Chinatown, and Nob Hill. You could even walk to Union Square. When we went in September, we spent a day in Napa Valley.The concierge helped us book a rental car for delivery at the hotel the next morning.However, when we went to the lobby the car wasnt there.Because it was Labor Day weekend, the rental car company was slammed.We understood and went to go pick up the car.To make a long story short, we ended up waiting 2hours in line, and it ruined the whole day for us.Although it wasnt The Omni's fault, when we returned that night, I informed the concierge and he took care of the valet.Upon returning home, I received the Omni Hotel survey,and let them know about the mishap.I promptly received a response from the hotel's general manager Carmen Serra and she apologized for the inconvenience the rental car company caused us,and refunded the rental car fee back to our credit cars.She also helped me book another stay at the Omni in San Diego for next weekend.I was very satisfied with how she handled the situation...just another reason why I love the Omni! No one is perfect, everyone makes mistakes, but I appreciated their efforts to resolve the issue.

I have stayed in nicer hotels, but this was in a good location to sight seeing and shopping. The rooms were quiet and the beds were confortable enough. We did, however eat at the restaurnant downstairs for dinner and breakfast and had some issues. The food was good, but the service was not. Waiters were slightly rude and one night at dinner we had to go find the hostess to be seated. We stood there for over 15 minutes. Across the street there is a stop for the trolley and the bellman was good about helping us hail taxis. One night they even had the hotel car take us to the pier for our alcatraz tour. Overall we had a good experience at this hotel and would recommend it to others.

<Author>CynthiaBG
<Content>Omni, Great Hotel! Stayed at the Omni from October 24th to October 29th. We arrived very late on the 24th and were thrilled at the quick and easy way the whole check-in process was handled. Everyone we came in contact with were very happy and willing to help you in any way they could. Need to make a reservation for dinner, day trip, tour? All you had to do was ask the people at the front desk and they were very happy to provide all the information you might want and and make the arrangements for you. Had a partial bay view room, very nice size, perfect size bathroom didn't have any complaints about that at all. The hotel is in walking distance to the ferries that will take you over to Sausalito. Union Square, and Chinatown are within walking distance too. If you needed to catch a cab all you had to do was ask one of the doormen and you had one in a flash. There are always town cars out front too if you prefer a little more plush ride somewhere, not much more expensive than a cab and a lot nicer. I have to say I don't know what anyone would have to complain about when staying at this hotel. Would certainly stay here again!

<Author>Frankie-and-Emma
<Content>Omni is very nice.... We spent 10 nights at the Omni in September and had a fantastic time. The hotel is convenietly located in the Financial district within walking distance of Union Square, Fishermans Warf etc. Our room on the 5th floor did not have a great view but was very quiet and well worth sacrificing the view for. The rooms are in excellent condition, and the maid service is first class. The staff are very helpul and courteous at all times, ensuring our stay went without a hitch. The only small complaint we have is that the one and only bar in the hotel (Bobs bar) is very small and gets very crowded from approx 5pm onwards, and getting a seat was almost impossible around those times. However it is no reason not to stay here. When we first arrived after our lengthy journey from Scotland, we were informed that our room (booked and paid for 8 months previousley) had been cancelled by Octopus travel who we had booked the room through. The hotel staff could not have been more helpful in rectifying the situation.San Francisco is well worth a visit and has plenty to offer for all. We would recommend visiting Alcatraz and taking the coach tour of the city, however book your Alcatraz tickets online as far in advance as possible to ensure you get the dates you require. We also hired bikes from Blazing Saddles and rode over the Golden Gate bridge to Tiburon via Sausilto. This is a fantastic way to see the bridge and surrounding area (weather allowing). Sausilto is a must see when you are there and can be accessed by Ferry if you prefer not to bike it, dining is recommeded at Angelino's while you are there. We also took a wine tour to Napa valley etc and would recommend this trip, with plenty of samples included in the day ensuring the hoilday spirit was flowing. Union square is packed with all the usual big name shops, but visit the hippy district at upper Haight street for some of the funkiest shops available. We visited the zoo but found it to be dated and shabby with many of the animals not available to view. Of course you must take a ride on a tram while you are there, we would advise getting a day pass for 11 bucks, which allows you to hop on and off all day at your leisure. Finally Lombard St aka the most crookidest street in the world is worth a look with camera in hand.We had 2 days of cloud followed by 8 days of glorious sunshine while we we there.Book it up, you will enjoy!!!!  
<Date>Oct 3, 2008

We were just as pleased with the hotel as the recent reviews and high ranking indicate.The Front Desk and Concierge were very pleasant and always willing to assist with questions. We had a great room with a very nice city view. Housekeeping was very detailed and the room was impeccably clean. I thought a very nice touch/detail was a personalized handwritten note from our housekeeper welcoming us. You dont see that too often.We did room service on Friday night and ordered off of the Bob's Steakhouse menu, which is the hotel's restaurant in the lobby. The food was awesome! The filet was so tender and by far the best baked potatoe and candied carrot I have ever had! The delivery was right on time, the food was hot and the server was very friendly. I travel alot for business and I find Room Service to be very poor even in the best hotels. Not here. They did a great job!They gym at this hotel is very nice with great cardio and weight machines. Little details like complimentary bottled water and a huge basket of fresh fruit are not forgotten.The location was very convenient and the price we paid was a bargain for the value and in comparison to most of the other hotels in the area since we shopped around before making our reservation. I highly recommned this hotel!

<Author>miabailey
<Content>Omni Very Nice Hotel We stayed at the Omni for 3 nights at the end of our Alaskan cruise. First impressions were great door men and bell boys and reception very helpful check in was quick and easy, and although we arrived early our room was ready.The lobby is very grand with a classy feel, we ate in the restaurant once for breakfast which was nicely presented although where service is concerned they seemed to focus more time on the business people than the people on vacation we didn't get as much attention as the business people.Our room was nice although we had a few problems phone would not stop beeping and was very loud and annoying,safe was broken and so was the plug in the sink. We reported these faults to the front desk straight away and these faults were dealt with immediatey. When I expressed my disspointment with the faults in our room Richard on the front desk was very apologetic but was unable to move us as the hotel was full due to the Oracle convention being in town but that he would report our concerns to his manager. That evening when we got back to our room there was a letter of apology and a free breakfast voucher which was a nice touch. Our room was spacious with a large flat screen t.v and large comfortable bed the bathroom was again very spacious and very clean.Its the small touches in this hotel that make your stay memorable the turn down service is exellent along with the usual chocolates ou also get a small card informing you what the weather will be like the following day. The location of the Omni is o.k in the financial district so not much around in the 1st few blocks but Union square in only a 15/20 min walk away but a taxi is necessary to Fishrmans Wharf which will cost just under $10.Despite the faults in our room on arrival the Omni is a very classy hotel and would definitely return to this hotel.

<Content>Efficient but not great value We stayed at this hotel at the end of a trip travelling around California. When we started our trip we stayed at the excellent Donatello, but unfortunately they had no rooms available when we returned to the city. The Omni was expensive and although it did everything it is meant to do it did it without any soul. We booked through Priceline a room with two double beds. On arrival Reception said that as this was booked through a third party it could not be guaranteed and so we had to have a bed made up for our daughter. I have no criticisms of the room, apart perhaps that everything being a bit too frilly - not really our style. I was irritated to have to pay $10 for access to the hotel wifi - why do the cheaper hotels and motels provide this free and the more expensive hotels charge for this?The breakfast was over formal and as their is no buffet we ordered dishes that were OK, but extremely over priced. The staff were efficient and the doorman friendly, but I would not stay at this hotel again.

<Author>Sus52
<Content>Great hotel, great location, great staff! Beautiful lobby - I was a little concerned when we arrived because I had booked a discounted rate through an online booking site and thought we might get an inferior room - but to my delight, we got a great room. The concierge was awsome, with details about restaurants (reasonably priced too!) and a great place for a drink with a view across the street. We were there on a Saturday when the hotel arranges a free 2 hr.morning walk with local historians. (different people each week) The hotel is located on the California cable car route (the front desk can sell you 1,3 or 5 day passes which cover all public transit and are a great value). Don't miss the cable car museum - free and really interesting - for kids from 1 to 100! Don't go for breakfast at the hotel - unless you want to pay $25 for bacon and eggs and don't drink the bottled water in the room - it had a price tag of $6.99 on it! Go to the fitness room where you can pick up a small bottle for free that fits nicely into your handbag! Also they have fresh fruit in the lobby - and if not there, then in the fitness room again! We would definitely recommend this hotel.

<Author>Cantjr5
<Content>Great hotel, great service I stayed at the San Francisco Omni twice during my 11 day trip to N. California. I have never stayed at an Omni, even though I travel 5-7 times a year. I loved this hotel, specifically because of its superb service. When traveling for pleasure I prefer BB because of the hospitality, local flavor, attention to service. I have to say that the folks at this Omni treated me and my wife as if we were at their home. We were always graciously greeted by the doorman, front desk, and concierge....they actually remembered us. It is such a surprise to get this level of attention in such a big city, in the heart of the financial district.The rooms were very, very clean. As I was there twice during my trip I was able to compare 2 different room types. Both times, the rooms were impeccably clean. All of the amenities you would expect for a business hotel are available. The hotel is located very close to the Ferry building and Chinatown. Being located in the financial district makes the hotel close to San Francisco's excellent restaurants including, Aqua and Perbacco. We ate at Perbacco and would recommend to anyone.We used the concierge services extensively and they were always courteous, quick, and thorough. It just wasn't the concierge that helped us. Everyone in the hotel goes out of their way to help. The lady that checked-us in, Crystal, was superb!!!They made a number of reservations for us and provided excellent recommendations.It's not close to the touristy areas near Fisherman's Wharf, but I wasn't looking to be in the heart of a tourist haven. If you are looking for a great hotel, with excellent service that makes you feel like you are at home this is the place to be. I will definitely be coming back to this hotel.

<Author>xgirl76
<Content>Great hotel in a great location We stayed at the Omni in July this year. It was our first trip to San Francisco, so we weren't sure of which area to stay in, but the Omni turned out to be perfectly located for us. It's in the Financial District, so it's quiet at night, but we felt perfectly safe walking there after dark. It's also on the cable-car line, within easy walking distance of Chinatown and the Ferry Building and if you don't mind walking a bit further, you can easily walk to the Union Square and Fisherman's Wharf areas from here. The hotel itself is lovely and the room was spacious, clean and comfortable. If I had to pick one thing to fault the room on, it would be the fixed-head shower. I didn't have a particular problem with it, but it was just ok - investing a little money in the shower would really bring it up to the standard of the rest of the accommodation. Staff at the Omni were very friendly and helpful, from check-in, where they offered to help us book any attractions we wanted to see, room service bending over backwards to make us happy when there was a slight problem with our order, the concierge recommending places to eat, right through to the doorman offering us the hotel car when we were leaving for the airport (at only $5 more than the taxi fare, this was a nice option). In addition, when we had an issue with the guests in the adjoining room holding an impromptu party late one night, hotel security dealt with it very quickly.We joined the Select Guest program online for free and this entitled us to complimentary tea, coffee, hot chocolate and juice every morning, as well as complimentary WiFi access and a daily newspaper. We ate breakfast twice in the hotel restaurant, which was somewhat expensive, but excellent quality and really tasty. There was complimentary fresh fruit (peaches, apricots, plums etc, not just standard apples) and juice or iced tea in the lobby every afternoon, which was nice when returning from sightseeing before going out to dinner. And the gym provided complimentary bottled water and apples and bananas too.Overall, we really enjoyed our stay here and will definitely return if we are ever in San Francisco again!

<Author>TwoHavlesofCoconuts
<Content>Nice, but not a wow This is the second time I have stayed at the Omni, both on business. The Omni is a nice 4 star hotel. The rooms and bathrooms are of average size, but quite adequate. The furnishings are in good condition except for the carpet which is very tired and in need of replacing. The worn state of the carpet really detracts from the rest of the room. The internet connection, although it uses a wire, was fast and reliable ($10/day). The staff was very friendly and helpful. For example, they set up transportation for me on multiple days without a hitch. The hotel food is only average in quality, but very expensive. The hotel is located not far from anything, but not close to anything either; a geographical compromise. I timed the walk to Union Square at 15 minutes via Montgomery, hang a right at Post (note this way is flat, no hills). San Francisco hotels are very expensive for what you get. The Omni is better than both nearby Hyatts. I would stay there again, but will likely try another hotel on my next visit.

<Author>Napalover8
<Content>Living Large In San Francisco! Giving this hotel 5 stars is easy with the type of service they deliver! I am a believer!I pulled up after a night at the newly finished J.W. Marriott hotel in Union Square, bad planning on my part. I was denied late check out and feeling a little green; I thought I would take my chances on an early check-in at the Omni. Having booked through Travelocity, my hopes were not high. I was greeted by the extremely efficient and professional Evelyn. She was kind, sympathetic and sincere. I was not a lesser human being for booking a discount room from an online service, hurray! I was feeling better. Evelyn clicked away on her keyboard and had me in a room within 10 minutes, my day was turning around. Enter Fernando, the very pleasant and chatty bellman that seemed to know everyone. He whisked my luggage away and we had a nice conversation. I arrived in the simple, yet elegant room to find a handwritten note from the housekeeper, Suyuak. I am a sucker for the personal touch. Slipping into a comfortable robe provided by the hotel, I decided to order room service, a Kobe burger would surely bring me around. The burger arrived and it was delicious! The meat was lightly spiced with a hint of pepper and the melted cheddar was just right! The fries were lightly spiced and delicious too. My high school reunion was 5 hours away and I was starting to feel human again. After a nice nap on the comfortable bed it was time to shower and head out for the evening. At the end of a long night, I decided to have a couple of classmates over to continue the reminiscing. I called over from the Sir Francis Drake where the reunion took place and asked room service to send a cart of refreshments up to my room. 30 minutes later when we all arrived, a beautiful cart with stemware, refreshments and snacks was waiting for us. Two thumbs up for Ms. Joanne, the goddess of In Room Dining that was running the floor solo and made this all happen. Mind you it was the manager the next day that told me Ms. Joanne had been alone, Ms. Joanne never complained or muttered a word. She made it all seem effortless. When it was time to turn in, I was so happy to have a minty treat on my pillow and turn down service. Most hotels in the four star genre have done away with this simple pleasure, it was a real treat to see my sheets folded down.When I walked up to the counter to check out the following day, I couldn't wait to shower the staff with praise. Crystal was checking me out and before she had the chance to ask, I blurted out I love this hotel! Crystal proceeded to check me out with the utmost efficiency and showered my with savings passes for Nordstrom, Bloomingdales and Macy's. What a smart move! Now I have to go back and book a room for a shopping weekend! All around the staff were magnificent, the hotel was well maintained and aesthetically pleasing, and I left in a really good mood!In the future I will book directly through the hotel and pay the higher price. I don't want to risk ending up at another hotel!

<Content>wonderful omni We had the pleasure of 3 nights at The Omni with our family of 4 including 2 teenage girls one of whom uses a wheelchair. The staff at the Omni could not have been more helpful and friendly and although there were not many families that we could see staying I highly recommend this place to families looking for an up market experience. <Author>mikekauffman
<Content>Excellent Stay at the Omni All of the prior reviews are true - the Omni is excellent. It may have been the nicest hotel we have ever stayed in - definitely in the top two. We stayed for two nights at the end of July. We had a 15th floor room with a partial view of the city. The rate we paid included valet parking for each night, normally an additional $48 per night charge. The room was large and very clean. The bathroom had a double sink with a very large countertop.The hotel was very convenient to Chinatown and Fisherman's Wharf. The entrance to Chinatown was only a short walk from the hotel and the cable car route to Fisherman's Wharf stopped right in front of the hotel. Our rental car was parked on Friday afternoon and we did not retrieve it until we left on Sunday.The service had the hotel was exemplary. Each employee we encountered was very friendly and helpful. The hotel concierge gave us a great overview of the area and the doormen provided excellent dining tips.As members of Omni's Select Guest program, we were treated with complimentary beverage service each morning, consisting of a pot of coffee and tea and a choice of several fruit juices, along with a choice of three newspapers. This service was very prompt - we requested 8:00 each morning, and the beverages arrived by 7:30. This service allowed us to enjoy our coffee and tea and newspaper before heading out to breakfast. Two excellent breakfast locations within walking distance were Lori's Diner and Sears' Fine Food.As several other reviewers mentioned, there is free bottled water and fruits available in the 3rd floor Fitness Center.One local feature not to be missed is the lounge located on the 52nd floor of the Bank of America building, located across the street from the Omni. The nighttime view of the city through the lounge's wall of windows was spectacular.

<Content>Our stay at the Omni was great! My best friend and I stayed 10 days at the San Fran Omni in late April 2008. It is a great hotel. It was very clean, the room was a nice size, bathroom was large, the staff was extremely friendly and helpful. There was internet available in the lobby for a fee. In the future, I will always look for an Omni hotel to stay at, especially when in a large city. It has a restaurant and a separate bar/grill also. The restaurant served huge portions, everything was cooked to perfection, we ate there twice during our stay. The bar/grill was nice also, nice menu selections, such as crab tacos (yum), burgers, sliced steak. It is in the financial district and on the cable car line also. Close to Chinatown. We also ate at Houston's, across from the Ferry Building, excellent, especially the ribs, it was pricey but well worth it. The highlights of the trip for us were Alcatraz tour, Napa Wine-tasting tour, and Monterey-Carmel tour.

<Content>Loved it! Fabulous Anniversary!!!! Everything was perfect from the time I made my reservations until the day we left. We made reservations to celebrate our anniversary and do a quick in-town getaway. The Omni is located in the financial district, but is close to many great neighborhoods. We were able to walk to the Embarcadero, North Beach, and Chinatown. It is also really close to public transportation, including BART and the Cable Car (for real tourists).Originally I was going to just spend one night in a suite, but the reservationist suggested that since we were coming for our anniversary, we consider their Hearts in San Francisco package. We decided to do this instead for 2 nights. It included a deluxe room with King bed, champagne and chocolates in the evening, and breakfast either at the restaurant on site or served in your room.I called ahead to see if they had any suggestions for a special anniversary dinner and they made us reservations at Aqua. We checked in online and simply had to pick up our keys and go straight to our room upon arrival. When we got to the room, housekeeping had put a heart of rose petals on our bed. Within 20 minutes our champagne and chocolates arrived. There was also a reminder letter with our key to give us directions to the restaurant which is only 2 blocks away. I also called for suggestions of somewhere to go after dinner and was given the perfect spot at the Bubble Lounge.The next day was just as wonderful and with the same treatment of the room the next night was completely romantic. Everyone at this hotel is friendly and helpful. It all started with Joey Nubla (concierge), to Darrell at the front door, to our bellmen Adam and Joey, our fabulous housekeeper Maria, the room service staff and John and Justin at the front desk. Thank you all for giving us the perfect getaway for our anniversary!

<Author>daverrco
<Content>I'll be back! From the moment the front door was opened on our way in to check in to the time the front door was opened on our way after check out, my girlfriend and I were treated like royalty at the Omni. I've been to San Francisco many times and the Omni is the BEST hotel I've stayed in. The service is exquisite. Everyone from the doorman to the front desk personnel to the housekeeping staff is exceptionally friendly, always upbeat, and very helpful. The hotel itself is very clean, elegant, and conveniently located close to Chinatown, North Beach, and the Financial District. The California Street Cable Car line runs past the hotel's front door, and the BART station is five blocks away. The room was large, clean, and well maintained. There was a nice flat screen TV and DVD player in our upgraded signature room, though not every room may be equipped similarly. Every morning our housekeeper would leave us a handwritten note wishing us a pleasant day. We'd write her back telling her of our travel adventures and leave her a well-deserved tip for her service. She even recommended a great place to try authentic dim sum! Staying at the Omni was definitely the key to a most enjoyable San Francisco adventure! I'll be back to San Francisco soon and, without a doubt, will be staying at the Omni again!

<Author>Irelandeye
<Content>Good hotel in central location We have stayed in the Omni San Francisco before so it was the natural choice for a return visit. The staff in general were helpful particularly the door men - it is nice to get the door opened for you! We had a few probs - the keys issued to our party did not open the doors and we were left standing on the corridor with our luggage whist the security checked our ID again before they could re-issue our cards - no proper apology from the reception desk as I would have expected. Also we had one of our rooms booked for three but only one king bed !- they sent up a rollaway - at no extra charge - I would hope so as we had paid for 3 people!We had booked a suite and a bedroom and they put us in the corner suite area which was very handy - suite was quite spacious - flowers in bathroom and fruit were supplied - nice touch. Beware double beds are tiny and really do not fit 2 people. Thet now charge for use of their internet business room - so take your laptop - it is free for 'select guests ' in the lobby - you can print airline boarding passes for free for a restricted number of airlines - but would be better if they had access to international ones as well! Overall a nice hotel - though like many hotels in San francisco it is quite pricey - SF hotels are pricier than NYC or Boston Breakfast is expensive for what you get - much better value in the Omni in Boston! - which is hard to beat for breakfast!

<Author>DebWaid
<Content>Beautiful hotel, great location! I just spent two nights at the Omni in San Francisco at the end of a 10-day trip to various California sites. We had three couples in our party. The hotel is beautifully decorated, had conscientious staff, great sheets. It's location is two blocks from Chinatown in the Financial District, and the street car runs right in front of the hotel. We needed quick transportation one evening in order to make our Alcatraz Tour, and the doorman provided two town cars for our party and we only had to tip the drivers. Because of its location, our 9th floor room overlooked the top of the Wells Fargo Bank and a Subway shop.There is a complimentary coffee maker in the room and a daily newspaper. We were very disappointed to be charged $10 a day for wireless internet access, since every other hotel we had stayed at in California provided this service for free.There is no parking. Valet parking service provided by the hotel is $48 a day plus tipping the driver! There is St. Mary's Parking Garage one block away with the awesome rate of $32 a day! The phone in the bathroom, lighted closet, and nightly turn-down service was nice.

<Author>cili_padi_nz
<Content>Good 4-star hotel in a great location We stayed at the Omni for 3 nights. Our room was available when we checked in at noon and we had a late check-out at 2pm. The check-in staff are friendly and very prompt. The room is a good size, the bed is comfortable, and the amenities are good. The decor is a bit tired, but clean and tidy. Wi-fi is $9.95 for 24 hours. There is a turndown service every evening, which is a very nice touch. The staff at the concierge desk are knowledgable and very helpful. They sell tourist muni passports which is excellent (1 day for $11), and a very helpful female staff showed us how to get to the various attractions. There is complimentary lemonade and fruit late afternoon in the lobby. The location is excellent. The Ferry Building to the right, Chinatown to the left and Union Square to the south. Tadich Grill, an SF institution is 4 blocks right of the hotel, and we stumbled upon it by a very fortunate mistake. Unwittingly, we were in SF for the Gay Pride parade, which we happily attended. The atmosphere was fantastic. We booked through Expedia.co.nz, and paid NZ$266 per night (including taxes) which was very reasonable.

<Author>BCCajun
<Content>20th Anniversary Stay was Terrific I have stayed in many hotels all over the world. The Omni service was exceptional which is why this hotel is so highly rated. The premium class room on the top floor (17th) was large with the usual first-class amenities - king size bed, armoire holding the TV - mini-bar-drawers for clothing, a writing table and a chair. The room was very much like other major UPSCALE hotel chains but nothing palacial. The room was accurately described as having a partial view so I was not expecting more than this. I could see the bay but I also saw a lot of the side of the L-shaped Omni itself. The only hotel that I saw there that I would like to investigate next time was the Intercontinental Mark (somebody). It is a high rise on Nob Hill which is elevated already so I am sure the views were pretty spectacular. I am sure the price is as well. We had brunch at the Top of the Mark which is - you guessed it - on the top floor and we saw the view ourselves. Spectacular. But back to the Omni...When we told the concierge that this was our 20th Wedding Anniversary, they immediately arranged to have champagne and chocolate covered strawberries delivered to our room - complimentary. Having a bottle of champagne around just changes the whole mood of a hotel room - I highly recommend it. I am not suggesting that you lie about it being your anniversary, though.I had the 3-1/2 days in San Fran very well scheduled before we arrived because I wanted to make the most of our short stay, so I took the wind out of the concierge's sails when I showed him my calendar chart of restaurant reservations, Alcatraz cruise, Wok Wiz Chinatown tour, etc, but I would have missed the opportunity of eating at the Slanted Door if the concierge had not pointed out that they were in fact open for lunch (I had seen information indicating they only opened at 5 and could not work it into our evening time slots.) Tiger prawns, Vietnamese crepes, beef short ribs. WoW!One complaint: when you stay at the hotel that is rated #1, any little thing that is wrong will seem like a big deal. For instance, I had to take the coffee service tray out of the armoire and set it on the table and then I had to crawl under the table to reach the electrical outlet just to get it plugged in. I found myself getting quite indignant (silly pride) at the effort I had to personally exert just to hook up the thing. I have done this before in other hotels and not been nearly as bothered. Lesson: limit your expectations and you will always be more satisfied.Also: This is in the Financial District. While we never felt like we were out of the main part of town, it does get quiet on weekends. This was pleasant to us. You are still only a few blocks from Union Square, the Ferry Building, and Chinatown and you have cable cars running directly in front of the hotel. You will not feel isolated in the least. The location was perfect and in no way diminished our stay.

<Author>Louis1ma
<Content>A few glitches - but nice My wife and I decided to take a long weekend, including a Monday off work, and spend it in San Francisco. We chose the Omni based on its reputation and location. Both lived up to expectations but for one glitch - the internet was down our entire stay.First the good. The location is perfect; in the heart of the embarcadero and financial districts and on the outskirts of China Town. You can easily walk to the farmers market (Sat and Tues), Coit tower, China Town, North beach or Union Square. The hotel staff were friendly and efficient and the Hotel was a pleasant level of old school; clean, comfortable and well cared for. We booked a signature room, which was a good size and high up on the 16th of 17 floors. Our package included parking and internet for $239 a night. Ask for this package when booking. The restaurant bar in the lobby, Bob's Bar (not the steakhouse) had great food and drinks and seems to be where locals and local business people hang out - it was fun.Now the minor bad - which left a bad taste. The internet, which they charge for in standard rooms and even the business center, was out all three days. Each time we called, the front desk gave us a differnt explanation and a different timeframe for its solution. We wanted the internet to search for restaurants, events and attractions. We also needed it to access our offices to justify a last minute day off. I asked if we could use the business office internet and they said sure, swipe your credit card Internet was free in our room but we had to pay - not cool.

<Author>StephNewZealand
<Content>A great hotel We had only two nights at the Omni in May. We were on our way home to NZ after 6 weeks travelling in Europe laden with luggage!What a pleasure it was to arrive at the Omni after negotiating the chaos of Los Angeles Airport! We arrived at 8.30 am and our room was not available but hotel reception couldn't have been more helpful in storing bags, offering bathrooms and recommending places for coffee or breakfast. The manager personally hurried up the availability of our room and had us safely ensconced by 10am.Our room was a standard king but so spacious by European hotel room standards. It was immaculately clean and well appointed. Our only negative comment would be that there was no kettle for boiling water for a cup of tea. There was a coffee maker available but to just boil water in that took forever! The bed was large and firm with comfortable pillows and crisp linen. Nice range of toiletries in the bathroom which were replaced twice daily if needed-a nice touch.Our room was facing into a central area so only view was of other buildings. The upside of this was that we got no road noise whatsoever-Lovely and quiet so would probably request same on return visit.Hotel is in financial area so if here on holiday as we were, not too many restaurants or cafes in the immediate vicinity. This was a bit of an issue especially as we were there on a Sunday night and a Monday which was a public holiday so virtually nothing around. North beach though is only a short taxi ride away.The strength of this hotel though was its outstanding staff. They were respectful, extremely helpful and willing to answer all queries and wishes in a friendly courteous way.Wold we stay here again?---A resounding yes.

<Content>Great Hotel, Great Location, Great Kids Room, Great City... A great classic and classy hotel. The service is outstanding. The atmosphere is luxurious, and extremely kid-friendly in a city that is not really kid-centric. We were lucky enough to book the Kid Fantasy Suite for my kids (ages 9 and 11) with an adjoining King room for my husband and I. While there is much more the decorators could have done to make it a true kid fantasy room, it made my kids feel like they were special. Bunk beds, bean bags and nightly milk  cookies -- what more could a kid want?! (Well, a pool would have been ideal, but they didn't mind too much).The restaurant in the hotel, Bob's Steak House, was fantastic. A little pricey, but typical for the city and the food was worth it. There are several outstanding restaurants within an easy two block walk of the hotel.We were there over a long weekend, and it seemed many cafes and smaller restaurants were closed for the weekend, or had very limited hours. (The closest McDonald's was completely closed on Sunday -- not a big deal unless you have a 9-year-old craving a Happy Meal)But the location was great in regards to the ease in getting to public transportation. Also, there are a ton of things within walking distance -- China Town, the Ferry Building, Union Square.The service at the Omni is wonderful! Everything from the front desk staff to the housekeepers to the room service attendants. I could go on an on about this hotel, but to simply summarize: if you are going to San Fran, stay here!

<Author>hatster31
<Content>Solid and convenient hotel I stayed at the Omni for 2 nights over Memorial Day weekend. I got a great weekend rate at $169 a night. LOCATION: The location could not be any better. We took the BART and walked 4 blocks (10 minutes) to the hotel. Just make sure you don't have too much luggage. The hotel is also within walking distance of Union Square and Chinatown. There are also Muni lines and cable car lines very close by.HOTEL:I knew that it was an older hotel, but I guess I expected the rooms to be nicer. It is very clean, but there was no wow factor that I have seen at other hotels like Novotel Singapore or Venetian in Vegas. It was a regular room with regular t.v. with nice amenities but nothing ultra-modern. The bed was very comfortable. The rooms were very quiet, although you could hear some hallway noise, but nothing from outside the building. I guess that is why they are not considered a 5 star hotel. Minus one star for the room.SERVICE:The service was very good overall. Check in was quick and all the staff were extremely friendly. We are a select guest, so we get morning beverage service (you are supposed to get a card outside your room and you hang it out with your beverages). Since this is our first stay, we had no idea how this worked. We never got a card and got no beverages in the morning. When I called the front desk, they forwarded me to room service, and I got my beverages. I also told front desk that I didn't get a beverage card, just a room service, when they asked if I hung it outside. Well, for a #1 rated Tripadvisor and 4 star hotel, I would expect a select guest beverage card the following night, but no. So, minus one star for that. However, when I wanted coffee the next morning at 11:00 a.m. (they have a pot of coffee in Bob's every morning until 10:00 a.m.), the staff got me one, so add one star.Overall, this is a great hotel with great service. I can see why it is not 5 stars, but the service really makes it above the rest.HOTEL TIPS:Get free water and fruit in the fitness room. There is also free fruit in the afternoon and free lemonade in the lobby. There is free coffee in the morning at Bob's bar until 10:00 a.m. But, you get free beverage service delivered to your room if you sign up as a selected guest.RESTAURANT TIPS:We found two great restaurants within walking distance of the hotel. Both are highly rated on yelp. The first is Bix. It is on Gold St., which is about 5 blocks north of Montgomery (10 minutes walk). It's in a small alley, and the food is awesome and moderately priced (entrees $25 to 35 range). Their appetizers are incredible, and the atmosphere is very nice. The second is Great Eastern in Chinatown for dim sum. This place is located on Jackson St. by Kearny. It is very clean compared to the other Chinatown places, and you order off of a menu with pictures (no carts). Service is a bit slow, but if you are looking for an adventure in Chinatown, definitely try dim sum there. Go early (before 11:00) to avoid the crazy crowds!  
<Date>May 27, 2008

<Author>Mamabear79
<Content>The Omni went above and beyond My best friend and I went to San Francisco for a girls weekend and had the best time. The hotel was fantastic. From greeting us with roses and first class service upon checking in, to our beautifully appointed room.  It was a deluxe room with two double beds, marble bathroom, with no real views but very comfortable. We are wary of hotels but felt right at home at the Omni, as everything was clean and comfortable. I have stayed in Fairmonts and nicer hotels, and I would say that this hotel was at par with a 4+ star, it was great. My girlfriend celebrated a birthday during our stay and we only mentioned it to the front desk clerk when asked why in town, after dinner one night they sent up a bottle of champagne, two small birthday cakes and a personalized card. It was perfect! The gym was great, tv's on all the equipment and was never full, or even half full. Get your water there as there is complimentary water, and the bottle in your room is $6. Oh and there is also fresh fruit in the gym, which might be a nice snack as the mini bar and room service are quite pricey. Which isn't too much of a problem since the Omni is near alot of nice cafes, restaurants etc. (right beside the Omni there is a cafe which has everything and makes delicious panini's.... which are worth the trip back to San Francisco). We never ordered anything from the hotel.... except a bagel and fruitplate in the morning.... and it wasn't outrageous. No pool, no views, but what the hotel lacks in those areas, it completely compensates for in friendly helpful staff. It is close to China town, Union square, North beach and across the street from the Carmelian room which has amazing views while you dine. Become an Omni select guest member (free online) and you can get a complimentary morning beverage and paper, turn down service and upgrade after so many stays. Being on California street, alongside the cable cars, the Omni makes it easy to get around without a rental car. I would actually say avoid renting one if possible as parking in San Francisco is expensive and hard to come by. The hotel charges $45 I believe. So we rented one to drive up to win country, and returned it the same day, just to save us the hassle of paying for parking and returning it the next day.  San Francisco is a fantastic city and the hospitality extends far beyond the hotels and tourist areas. Everyone is so nice and made our trip so enjoyable. The Omni is a great hotel in a great location. We will return and as soon as we can.  
<Date>May 9, 2008

<Content>Delightful hotel in a great location We spent four nights at this delightful hotel at the beginning of April. When we arrived we had to wait about 5 mins before the check-in staff were able to attend to us and this resulted in my wife being given a rose and also an upgrade to a very comfortable suite. Although the hotel is in the financial area which is a bit quiet at the weekend, it is ideally situated for most of the tourist areas. Public transportation is also very accessible from the hotel.The hotel has a very pleasant restaurant and bar, however I feel the cost of the meals in the restaurant was a bit excessive and the signature giant honey glazed carrot which seemed to accompany most of the meals was a bit wasted on us. On the last night we decided to stay in the bar as we had spent the day on a very enjoyable wine tour to the Napa valley. On this occasion we chose a bar meal which was extremely tasty and far better value for money.Although the cost of the rooms is expensive during the week, it is possible to get a good deal for Fri/Sat/Sun nights but I would recommend contacting the hotel directly. I would certainly stay at this hotel again and would recommend it.

<Content>Loved the Omni San Francisco I really enjoyed my 2 night stay at the Omni last weekend. <Author>TXBluebonnet
<Content>Good stay at the Omni Stayed Saturday night, the first day of our vacation at the Omni. Our room was on the 6th floor overlooking California St. It was quite comfortable and quiet although I don't know if it would be as quiet during the work week with much more traffic going by. Easy walk to Chinatown and the financial district. The California Cable car line runs right in front of the hotel. Easy connection to the Hyde and Powell line which takes you to Fisherman's Wharf area, Chinatown and Lombard Street. You can buy a day pass at the front desk. Our $200 rate included a Deluxe Room and valet parking ($45 otherwise.) and we thought this was reasonable for San Francisco. We were quite comfortable during our stay.

<Author>CaTraveler7777
<Content>Pleasant stay We spent a long weekend at this hotel and found it to be a very pleasant place, particularly for San Francisco. Everything is gleaming, and in good taste. The staff is excellent; when we asked to have the feather pillows and feather blanket removed due to my wife's allergy, someone was completed the task rapidly and pleasantly. The location is great, with about a bazillion restaurants an easy walk from the hotel. The concierge knows what he's talking about and was very helpful. The apples and apple cider available in the late afternoon was very welcoming. You get street noise if your room faces california Street, so I would ask for a quiet room in the back and/or a room on the top floors. I would also self-park at the St. Mary's garage a very short walk away to avoid the steep valet parking charge.

<Author>jgenyuk
<Content>Great deal for the money We stayed in Omni for 2 nights during spring break. They upgraded us to 16th floor which was supposed to have free internet but it was not clear how to get this and we got free internet through their Select membership (another great tip from TripAdvisor), it was spotty but not too bad. The room was not big but nice. Comfortable beds, outstanding linens and blankets. The shower pressure was good too. Nice touches like chocolates, bathrobes, good San Francisco map in the room. I tried to share the bed with my 6 year old, but didn't sleep well, and on the second night I requested a rollaway bed. It was also very nice and they didn't charge us for it. The toilet paper holder broke but was promptly fixed. We didn't go to the restaurant, too expensive. Cafe de la Presse, recommended by one of the reviewer, is a nice spot for breakfast, or you can walk to the Ferry building marketplace.All in all, I might have given it 4 stars if we had really paid the average price listed here, but we paid only $144 a night through Expedia, and compared with other CA hotels where we stayed during this trip for similar price, Omni was clearly in a different league.

<Author>france200710
<Content>Nice, but.... We stayed at the Omni for two nights (3/20  3/21) and were immediately impressed by the service upon our arrival. Also, the lobby of the hotel was magnificent. We had a Deluxe Room/Parking arrangement which was very economical ($200 per night plus Expedia fees which were a little high) and our request for a quiet room was certainly honored. The downsides: while the staff at the Omni is Excellent (with a capital e), it is obvious that they've been a victim of the more with less phenomenon currently plaguing the U.S. There was a false fire alarm which occurred which, while not they're fault, delayed our sightseeing as we had locked our camera in our room safe and the safe refused to open. When we informed the front desk, they assured us security would be up shortly. This took almost half an hour and two more calls. It would have been much better if we'd been kept advised as to the progress of security. More importantly, though, it would have been much better if there had been more than one security person available. This became a recurring theme of our stay. We had plumbing issues and it took, again, about half an hour for someone to come. I asked the front desk about whether one of our bags had arrived; they said they'd call me to advise me. When I never got a call, I had to call them again and inferred, from the desk clerk's apology, they'd forgotten to call me.Lastly, while our room was quiet, it was a bit run-down (carpet frayed/stained); is this how these discount rooms become available to the common masses?

<Author>DesignrLA
<Content>Why I'll never stay at another Omni Hotel Just a short note to explain to you why I will never stay in another Omni Hotel.I reserved a Signature Room at the Omni San Francisco Hotel through Hotels.com for 4 nights, arriving August 31 and leaving September 4, 2007.When I arrived at the hotel I was informed that they had over-booked their rooms. I was told that I would be put in a lower cost standard room, a room without the Signature Room complimentary services. Needless to say, I was not happy about paying the Signature price for the lower cost room, this because I had paid in advance.When I complained, I was offered a free breakfast. After I refused to accept the room they had offered, I was finally given a Signature Room. No doubt some other poor schmuck got stuck paying top dollar for a standard room. A first-class hotel would never have suggested downgrading a paying customer, regardless of how or how much they paid. But then, Omni isn a first-class hotel.Once I had checked into my Signature accommodations, everything was fine except for one minor detail. On Monday morning, September 3, while entering the bathroom in my suite, I stepped on a carpet nail that was protruding upward out of the carpet in front of the bathroom door. I didn think I needed to be concerned about walking barefoot in my own room, not in a first-class hotel.I wasn as angry about being injured by Omni negligence as I was by their response. When I contacted the front desk and explained that a nail had punctured my toe and that I was bleeding profusely, their staff offered me a band-aid. Given the fact that I was in pain and limping, given the fact that I now had to contact my doctor to find out when I last had a tetanus shot, given the fact that I now had to worry about catching some horrible disease from the last person who impaled themselves on their carpet nail - I would have expected a first-class hotel to be more consolatory than to offer me a band-aid.After I returned to my room, the Omni staff sent me a note stating that they were unable to find the nail that had injured me. They insisted that I point out the nail to their building engineer, which I did. As their building engineer was pounded the offending nail back into the floor, he stated that he discovered 2 more nails protruding upward out of the carpet in the same general area. I wasn aware that I was entering a ine field?when I checked into the Omni hotel.But the final straw occurred as I was checking out of the hotel. The desk clerk inquired as to my stay. I explained the whole sordid tale, the nail, the blood, the limping, everything. I then asked what was the best way to get to the Oakland Airport. To add insult to injury, she suggested that I walk 4 blocks to the BART station.Once I returned home, I contacted the Omni management to complain. The hotel manager promised to send me a voucher for several free nights stay. This never happened. A first-class hotel manager would have been a man of his word.But then, Omni isn a first-class hotel.

<Author>FanFicGuru
<Content>They surpassed my expectations! I wrote a review recently regarding my stay last year in September and as you can see, the experience was amazing. After such a great stay I knew that I had to come back to the Omni, and I am so glad that I did. Let me share my wonderful weekend with you.We came to celebrate my fiance's birthday. I made sure to let the Omni know during my reservations and when I spoke with the concierges to arrange for some cider to be sent up to the room. On our way to the hotel I realized we would like a DVD player in our room and when I talked with them I was informed that we wouldn't have to worry about asking for a DVD player because we had been upgraded to a suite (which included a DVD player)! The weather was pretty nasty the day we arrived, but we made it there (sopping wet, but still...). Greeted warmly by the door-man I got my keys and we headed to our suite. It was on the 7th floor, and at first I was disappointed because I had requested a high floor, until I opened the door to our room.The suites have a separate sitting room with a couch and two sitting chairs, as well as a desk and entertainment system set-up (I will post pictures shortly after the review is posted). The stereo was turned on, playing some soft classical music as we entered the room. The ambiance was magnificent. On the table were THREE separate greeting cards, wishing warm birthday wishes to my fiance', inviting us to ask for anything we need to be comfortable, as well as a personally written greeting card from the general manager! This is why the Omni San Francisco won top honors for best service in the United States! Within minutes of settling in there came another knock at the door. My fiance' and I were both surprised to see in-room dining had sent up a slice of chocolate birthday cake! It was very good and we were wondering if they planned to spoil us rotten all weekend. While there were no more additional amenities, the Omni, as always, was very fast and professional with any and all requests that I made. The night that we arrived, for example, I called the front desk to ask for recommendations for a good italian restaurant. The concierge I spoke to (Justin I believe was his name) was very friendly and recommended the North Beach restaurant/area, stating that there were numerous italian restaurants in the area that we could choose from. We took him up on it and sure enough we found a charming little place called Franchino's to have dinner. Our room also came with free breakfast each morning we were there. I've heard mixed reviews about the restaurant from other people, but I thought that the breakfast was very good. Granted that it came with my room and I didn't have to pay anything except for the tip. I'm not sure I would say the same if I actually paid the 25 dollars for the breakfast. Still, as an amenity to a hotel-room package, the breakfast is very good.If there was one thing that I had to say that was not the best experience during this last stay, it was that Cabs were hard to come by this time. I heard something about local taxi services boycotting the Omni, but I'm not sure if that was true or not. Whatever it was, many cabs dropped off their customers and just sped off rather than pick up people waiting in the cab line. So, my fiance' and I did a lot more walking than we probably planned to.Still, if you requested a copy of the 2007 rewards for hotels, you will see the Omni San Francisco won a number of honors. Ranking in at #34 worldwide in Luxury hotels, #3 in U.S Luxury Hotels, Best in the San Francisco Destination (of the top 25), #4 in World- Customer Service and #1 in U.S- Customer Service. That's not the chain, it's this branch! To any Omni San Francisco staff reading this review, thank you so much for making my stay so memorable and I can't wait to come back and visit you again.To anyone visiting San Francisco in the near future: Make your reservations! I can't stress enough how great this hotel is. Affordable luxury, amazing customer service and a great location makes the Omni San Francisco your best bet in this very large city.Happy travels!

<Author>Brian-SK
<Content>Very Good I stayed here for two nights in Jan 08 on the way home from a business trip. The reception was excellent, rooms and bahrooms are very good indeed and all the staff set out to please. Its a bit away from the main tourist areas (Union Square and the Wharf) but thats no bad thing. Its a 10 min walk to Union Square, and approx a 30 minute walk to Fishermans Wharf through North Beach. Its also about 10 mins walk to the Ferry Builiding where you can pick up the F Line tram. The California line cable car stops outside the door so transport is not a problem if you don't want to walk. I booked through the hotel web site directly as this offered the best deal ($169 per night) I also ate at Bobs Steak and Chop House (the hotel restaurant) on the first night. Very good but not a cheap option (approx $70-$80 a head for two courses and a couple of drinks). San Francisco is a great city and I would certainly stay here again.

<Content>I Love This Hotel!! This hotel  its' staff gives hotels a good name. It is why i love hotels; the staff is friendly/helpful/courteous/kind ( probably thrifty, brave, etc) from the desk staff to the concierge, bellmen, doormen  maids. The parking is a block or 2 away but only had to wait 5-10 minutes for the car to be brought around.The area has expensive restaurants (Tadich grill, cafe tiramisu) and less expensive ones (House of Nanking); a terrific place for breakfast is Cafe de la Presse a couple of blocks away--reminds me of Paris. You can walk to everything. I want to go again!

<Author>AjasTravels
<Content>Great stay at the Omni My fiance and I stayed at the Omni for 1 night. I found the cheapest rates on the Omni Hotel's website. Unfortunately nothing else was cheap. $45/night for parking with unlimited in and out privileges. $70 for a steak. $34 for 3 cocktails. $70 for 3 mediocre martinis and 2 appetizers. The onion rings were pretty bad. There is free wi-fi in the lobby, but $10 for an internet connection in your room. The hotel was beautifully decorated for the holidays. All of the staff were very nice and courteous when we arrived. Security was very helpful when my fiance got locked in the stairwell (you can get into the stairwell, but you need a key to get onto the floors). There was complimentary hot cider and cookies for the guests in the lobby. I especially liked the gingerbread men. The rooms were very nice and spacious (for SF) with marble countertops and high thread count bedding. I loved their bathrobes. When we went back to our room at the end of the night the maid wrote a welcome note and left mint chocolates on the nightstand. The hotel is located in the Financial district so lots of people go to the lobby bar after work. It's a few blocks from Union Square so we took a cab to get around town. I would have given the Omni 5 stars but some of the rates for food were ridiculous and the maids knocked on our door 4 times to clean the room.

<Author>OperaOnTheTurnpike
<Content>A great choice, whether you're there for business or for romance It may sound a bit strange, but I think it's true. Perfect for business and for romance too (not so for singles, partiers, families with kids and so on).Elegant, quiet, perfectly located in a very good part of town ... I think the Omni really has it all. It's obsviously not an inexpensive choice, but their rates are very reasonable for what you get.The lobby is beautiful and the rooms extremely clean, quite large and very comfortable, with incredible beds and bathrooms wonderfully appointed with marble and green and black granite. Room service was very good and front desk staff was efficient.One of the definite pluses of the hotel is the express check-out. So efficient, as you bypass the usual check-out procedures (unless you disagree with the price to pay). You gave them your credit card when checking-in, so finding your final bill in an envelope at your door room the final morning and simply leaving is always a great thing.The restaurant is average and quite overpriced, but I guess this is somewhat usual in this kind of properties. It was definitely what I like the least. You don't need to pay such prices for breakfast or dinner, especially considering you will find plenty of fantastic places to eat at reasonable prices in nearby North Beach and all over the city.The location is the very best I could personally ask for. I understand that those who visit San Francisco for the first time usually prefer to stay in Union Square (which, by the way, is within walking distance) or in Fisherman's Wharf (which I would never recommend), but, for me, the area around the Omni is the very best. for the following reasons:a) The area is very nice and you're within walking distance to places such as Union Square, North Beach, Chinatown, the Embarcadero, the cable car turntable, and so on.b) It is very quiet, as it is located at the edge of the financial district.So, when I have enough budget for it, the Omni is, for all those reasons and more, my personal choice in San Francisco, my very favourite city.

<Author>nitehawk
<Content>Our 3rd stay Superior hotel, beautifully decorated for Christmas. As stated, this was the 3rd stay at the Omni for my wife and I, stayed Dec. 15 - 19. We love San Francisco, the bay, the Pacific Ocean, The Golden Gate Bridge and staying at the Omni. Central, quiet and secure location in the financial district with a superb staff that starts with the doorman and includes all levels of staff and service personel. Rooms are fairly spacious (375 - 400 sq ft) and very comfortable. Stayed in a Signature room, which are located on the 16th floor. The hotel bar on the first floor looks out on the corner of California and Montgomery streets and can be crowded and noisey, but after 7p the business crowd moves on and it becomes an intimate spot to spend the evening and enjoy a gargle or two or three with the wife. Always treat ourselves to a dinner at Bob's Steakhouse. The steaks are outstanding, but as others have commented, the default vegatable is a giant cooked, glazed carrot, which is great if you like cooked carrots. I don't, so just order sans the carrot. Carrots aside, wouldn't even consider staying anywhere else in San Francisco.

<Author>Spook55
<Content>Great hotel for an anniversary stay My husband and I decided to splurge on a nice hotel for our third wedding anniversary. We live only an hour from San Francisco, but wanted to eat a nice dinner there, plus we had tickets for a football game the next afternoon. We got a decent price for a one-night stay, and we got more than our money's worth at this very luxurious hotel! The staff was incredibly friendly, the standard room was very comfortable, and it's an overall beautiful place. I liked the complimentary bath robes, and the toiletries in the bathroom smelled wonderful! The bar/lounge is nice, although the bartender on shift at the time was a little stiff. Check-in was quick, although we checked in online ahead of time and they didn't have our folio ready. Loved the warm apple cider and cookies they had available for guests downstairs! The hotel is in a great location near Union Square, although we didn't do any sight-seeing since we just had dinner and the football game in mind for our stay. I can't speak to the restaurant (we had breakfast at Starbucks a couple of blocks away) or the business traveler amenities, but I'm sure they're quite nice.NOTE: Parking is a MAJOR expense at San Francisco hotels, and this one is no exception! We did our homework and found a 24-hour city lot one block up the street to park our car - St. George's Square lot, I believe. We only paid $7 for the night (although I think the cashier made an error...it still would have been cheaper than the $45 the hotel would have charged us for valet).

<Author>HotelLuvvingFamily
<Content>Hotel stay part was great, marred by concierge and steakhouse We were there the day after Thanksgiving. It had a nice upscale feel for a reasonable rate of about $160 for a regular room (Thanksgiving weekend). Perfect if you want something nice that is kid friendly. Our family had a room, and the other family we were traveling with had 2 rooms with connecting doors. Both of our families have children ages 5 to 11. We loved the pretty hotel, decked out for the holidays. We loved its proximity to Chinatown (5 mins walk), and around 10 min walk to Union Square. It was a block away from a Walgreens and McDonalds, which is convenient if you have kids. The children loved their Omni backpacks and the complimentary milk and cookies. The staff is nice and attentive, they clean the room 2x/day. Downside is the concierge. They gave wrong information on restaurants twice - once they gave the wrong address to a restaurant they recommended at the Fisherman's Wharf. Another time they assured (and refused to double check) that a restaurant will be open for Thanksgiving dinner. When we got there, the restaurant was closed. They also were not aware of a fun pack that the Omni loans to kids that contains games and activities and such.For the restaurant in the hotel, Bob's Steakhouse... It was ok. One thing a steak purist would frown on is that the steak comes to you with a humongous giant single carrot right in the middle of the plate as if it is the main dish. The steak and the potatoes are to its left and right. Also, the carrot was dripping in glaze that contaminated our steak. When we inquired about this, they said that it is a Bob's Steakhouse signature (putting the carrot in the middle), but you can always ask to put it on the side.

<Author>Empathology
<Content>Excellent service This is an excellent quality hotel right in the heart of SF. The service from all staff was superb, location good, bar  restaurant great and so on!!This was just a quick one night stay before flying back to Europe. I was intrigued by the most romantic hotel in SF label when searching as we were at the end of our Honeymoon. Truth is it's a chain hotel that pretends not to seek out the corporate clients even though there were plenty of them. However, unlike so many other big name chains, the Omni seems to treat it's private guests very specially going that little step further for customer service. (Too often I find the chains trying to get the corporate money and just neglect those of us that want a nice hotel).Lots of nice little touches too numerous to mention here means I shall return here (and to any other Omni).And was it romantic? - Well this is not a boutique hotel - it's a large-ish city centre hotel. But given those constraints - surprisngly yes!  
<Date>Nov 8, 2007

<Author>Indianpass
<Content>Great Rooms, Great Management, OK Location (for us) We stayed at the Omni based on reviews and overall pricing compared to other similarly rated large Hotels in San Francisco. We arrived quite late on a Thursday evening (9:30pm Pacific) due to our flight from Atlanta. We had booked online and I had asked for an upper level no-smoking room. There was no availability for either unfortunately I was told and initially we were placed in a smoking-permitted floor and room. I called the front-desk to ask if any accomodation could be made. The night manager, a wonderful person named Ellen K., indicated she would have us moved to another deluxe room that was non-smoking if we didn't mind moving to another room on our third day/night's stay. This was fine with us. Ellen subsequently called back a few minutes later and said the third night would be an upgraded deluxe suite room on an upper floor because of the trouble (at no extra charge of course). The entire stay was extremely nice, the BellHop area held an extra bag for us for three days while we went to Big Sur in a Miata and provided the bag as needed. Overall a great customer service environment. And the rooms/beds/furnishing was top-notch. The only possible knock is that the hotel is in the financial district. The night-life areas, such as Union Square and North Beach, are within a few blocks walking distance so this is a minor point-of-note. Don't wear heels like my wife did though.

<Author>jke79
<Content>Horrible Experience with the Management My stay at the Omni San Francisco started out poorly when I requested a double room (with two double beds) but received a queen room (with one queen). I asked for a rollaway bed, and ages later received a ridiculous inflatable bed not suitable for a comfortable night sleep. I managed, but it was very uncomfortable. The worst part, however, came after my stay when I had a $300 charge on my credit card. I called to inquire about the charge and they proceeded to tell me it was for room damage. I had no idea what they were talking about and after further investigation, they told me there was a hole in the wall of the room we stayed in. I of course asked for the manager to call me, and was extremely taken aback at how I was treated. He was pompous and rude and immediately accused me of putting the hole in the wall. He assured me there was no way his staff would have missed the hole and rented out a room in such a state. I told him that they did, and that my friend (who I immediately phoned afterwards) actually saw the hole ?but forgot to mention it to me (it was at the bottom of the wall near the baseboard in the hallway near the door, making it easy to miss). After I relayed this to the manager, he made a snide remark about how guests of his hotel are high-class and would call and complain if they received a room with a hole in the wall. Having no idea of the consequences of not reporting the hole, my friend didn't feel he needed to say anything and thus I never knew about it. The manager was horribly condescending and from his last remark implied that I was not a high-class guest and idn belong?at his hotel. I again assured him that the hole was not from me and he had no proof. He again insisted that his staff does not make mistakes and would never rent out a room with a hole in the wall. I was not going to budge and insisted that he reverse the charge. After going back and forth for awhile, he finally succumbed and reversed the charge. However, I was left with a bad taste in my mouth. I should not have had to defend my honor, and I knew he thought I was lying even after he reversed the charge. Even though I got the charge reversed, I still didn feel like I won. This hotel should not be four-star, as four-star hotels would never treat their guests like this. The Omni San Francisco is a third-rate hotel with mediocre customer service and horrible management. Yes, it was bad luck that I got that room, but my experience with the management was enough to make me write this review and encourage travelers to stay somewhere else.

The price is so affordable that you really don't expect to be 'wowed' by the hotel. But our expectations were far exceeded.The service of every staff member we came in contact with was exemplary. The Front Desk personnel were so helpful in recommending restaurants, transportation, etc. They even booked a (future) dinner for us at a restaurant in Napa Valley, which was the next leg of our vacation.The Front Desk personnel, Bellboys, the Doormen, the Housekeeping staff---every single person treated us like royalty. Our room was perfectly clean when we arrived, the front desk staff went out of their way to see that we had a room with a view, and they always followed up by phone to make sure we received whatever service we had requested. Additionally, the location of the Omni is ABSOLUTELY excellent. We walked EVERYWHERE. To the Ferry Building every day, to Pier 39, Fisherman's Wharf, to Ghiaradelli Square, to Lombard Street, to dinner each night. We never had to take a taxi or other type of transportation. Granted, some of the walks were steep uphill climbs, but that was part of the inate charm of the city. What a fantastic, albeit short time we had in San Francisco. And many thanks to the Omni for making our stay so thoroughly enjoyable. Steve and Tammy Lunn, Laytonsville, Maryland  
<Date>Sep 15, 2007

<Author>noelmal
<Content>Great location The hotel had a great location - we walked to North Beach, China Town, the Ferry building and shopping in downtown and felt safe in the area. They switched out their room service menus 1/2 way through our stay and the prices went from reasonable to pretty expensive. R/S was always on time and they were friendly.Our room was small with two double beds, one chair and a desk but it was well kept and housekeeping was very good. Our room was by an elevator on the 8th floor so I was a bit worried that it would be noisy but it was very quite. Service was good in the hotel but sometimes the door staff was a bit too casual.We ate one night in the bar off of the lobby and the food was good as was the service. We also ate at the Market Bar down by the Ferry building twice - once for lunch and once for brunch. It was great and had inside and outside seating available. The Ferry building also had some great gourmet food stores and retail shops. We had dinner at Home in the Lower Haight area and it was very good. It had simple food and a nice atmosphere.Overall the hotel was a great jumping off location to most points in the city and it was a hassle free stay in a safe location.
