<Author>cosmic_charlie
<Content>Perfect Service at the Omni We stayed at the Omni San Francisco for 3 nights at the Labour Day weekend.It was the last stop of our honeymoon to the US and we couldn't have made a better choice.We were upgraded to a Bay View Room on the top floor (17th floor).My wife was given a rose at check in, they brought us a bottle of champaign and chocolate-coated strawberries and had arranged our bathrobes with another rose the first evening.Room service was simply outstanding.I highly recommend joining the free OMNI Select Guest programme which entitles you to complimentary WIFI, beverage and newsparer service.Staff was charming, attentive and helpful with the exception of one gruffy bellman.Dined once at Bob's Steakhouse (belonging to the hotel), waiters so so, but great food, had a perfect filet mignon.Cable Car line runs just in front of the house.The only minor drawbacks:- WIFI service doesn't work on the 17th floor which they somehow forgot to mention at check-in (however, as Select guest you can use the cable internet free of charge)- walls are quite thin (the same old story everywhere...)- parking: as usual in SF, street parking is a mess and the hotel charges a hefty 40$ valet fee for 24 hours + 6$ city tax.Hotel is within walking distance of Ferry Building, Embaracadero, Coit Tower, Market Street, Chinatown and SOMA.Would highly recommend and always return there.

<Author>tequila2000
<Content>Travel Agent's review My husband and I just returned from a wonderful 4 nights at the Omni, and have nothing but good things to say about the hotel.Arrival - we opted for public transportation, taking the BART from SFO airport to Montgomery st and walked up the street to the hotel (maybe a 10 minute walk) It cost us $5.15 per person rather than $42 for a taxi from the airport, and it took about 40 minutes.Check in/out - I had notified the hotel that we would be arriving early (10am) and we received our room right away. We were also permitted to check out late, at 1pm.Staff - were fantastic, very friendly and helpful. I had notified the hotel that it was my husband's birthday, and they sent up a bottle of wine (which was pretty good), a fruit and cheese platter and a birthday card. We had nightly turndown service and were given a weather report for the next day, and chocolates.Room - beautifully decorated room, comfortable king size bed, nice ammenities in the bathroom. There was a desk and an armchair with an ottoman - perfect for relaxing and putting your feet up after a long day of walking!Location - in the financial district, but within walking distance to all the sights (if you like to walk!) The hotel is very close to North Beach (Little Italy) and China town, where we enjoyed a few meals. The ferry building/market was a short 10 minute walk, and pier 39  Fisherman's Wharf were about a 25-30 minute walk away. We walked everywehre, and never found anywhere too far or more of a 1/2 hour walk. Concierge gave us maps and directions to all the places that we wanted to visit. There were also a few good nightclubs and pubs just around the corner from us.* Sign up for the free Signature guest program - you get juice and a paper every morning and nightly turndown service with a chocolate!Sights / recommendations* Alcatraz - we did the night tour (booked in advance), it was cool, and kinda spooky to be there at night.* Pier 39 - the sealions were one of our highlights, you could watch them play / fight for hours! We ate at Bubba Gump's (just for the novelty of it) but the food was lousy and overpriced.* Fisherman's Wharf - nice to walk around, lots of souvenir shops and fresh seafood stands.* Giradelli Square - go for the sundaes, they are worth the $8!* Lombard St - worth the walk up this hill / crooked street* Tonga Room - just up the street (hill) from the hotel (at the Fairmont Hotel) we went for the $8 happy hour buffet, well worth a visit for an early dinner, and the atmosphere is pretty cool, especially when it rains.* AT  T park - saw a Giants game (bought tickets there), what a nice park, with beautiful views of the bay (if you get the right seats - we were on club level)* Ferry Building / Market - there was always some kind of street performance going on there.We'd definately return to the Omni!  
<Date>Sep 11, 2007

<Author>MrsGWolverhampton_Uk
<Content>Elegant hotel and amazing steak restaurant! We stopped here for three nights as part of our honeymoon. The hotel looks very elegant and the front desk staff are extremely welcoming. They are very happy to offer you advice about 'the sights' and will make every effort to make you feel a valued customer. The price, which is not excessive, was justified in the quality. I'd told them that it was our honeymoon when I booked the room. When we arrived we had been upgraded to a beautiful room on the 16th (out of 17) floor. When we got to the room we were greeted with huge strawberries dipped in dark chocolate, chilled sparkling wine, red wine, fresh fruit, mineral water all dressed with orchid heads and a hand written note congratulating us. It was really wonderful.The room was a very good size, bathroom fantastic - Molton Brown products. Bed was extremely comfortable with very good quality linen. The whole hotel was very clean and the housekeeping staff clearly took pride in their work. There was even a note welcoming us to the hotel from the member of staff responsible for our room- very nice touch.We had breakfast and dinner in Bob's Steakhouse. The breakfast was nice but nothing outstanding. Service on both occasions was good. The steak however was simply the best either of us have ever tasted! We both had the fillet mignon, it was cooked perfectly to our request. Fabulous.I would definitely recommend this hotel and I will happily book hotels within this chain again.

<Author>BayAreaNative
<Content>Easy walk to various sites: Union Square by muni, cable car, BART After reading the glowing reviews on TripAdvisor, we used HotWire for our one night at the Omni, at a reasonable rate. (less than $200). We experienced the same outstanding service as previous posts mentioned, so I will try not to repeat information, except to recognize our concierge Justin Seeto who sent chocolate-covered strawberries and champagne to our room while we were out, to congratulate us on our anniversary.We called the Front Desk to thank him for the treats. Later, (most likely) our concierge also surprised us with a small bottle of wine, along with more chocolates, probably delivered during turndown service.I had also signed up for Omni's free Select Membership benefits online: i.e.complimentary morning newspaper - notify Front Desk which one, complimentary morning beverages - write on Breakfast menu tag and hang outside door before going to sleep, late check out - after 12 noon but notify Front Desk, evening turndown service, etc.We parked at St. Mary's Garage (entrance on left-side, 1/2 block before California, while driving north on Kearny). $32 for 24 hrs. No in-out privileges, but we didn't need our car since we could take public transportation everywhere, or walk a few blocks to Union Square/Chinatown/North Beach/Market St.We walked less than 10 min. to the Embarcadero stop on the F line (SFMTA's Muni ) to Pier 29/Chestnut St. to enjoy a dinner  show at Teatro Zinzanni. We enjoyed this European-style cabaret, focused on fun through comedy, music, Cirque du Soleil-style feats, audience participation/interaction, and a 5-course dinner. Since the seats are arranged in concentric circles, all views are good. We hardly noticed that 3 hours had passed when the show ended as we ate dessert.We also saw the da Vinci exhibit at the Metreon (4th/Mission, south of Market), closing Dec. 31. The range of inventions displayed and re-created was astounding, especially the precursors to modern inventions. If you show a BART ticket until Aug. 31, you get a $4 discount off the adult admission price.We may take our kids next time for an Omni stay, or go by ourselves again!

<Author>MineralKing
<Content>Lots of Class From the minute you step into the lobby and the eager (but not overly) front desk staff greet you, you know you're in for a great stay.The lobby is beautiful with seating areas for cocktails or dining... all sparkling and impressive. Great steakhouse and bar located in the hotel too...Right on California Street on the Nob Hill cable car line, you can close the double glazed windows and not hear a thing, or slide em up a little for some ambient SF street noise... it's great.The room I had was a king bedded room in front of the hotel on the 11th floor with a view of the Bank of America building. Great pillows! Firm but comfortable bed. The bathroom was marble and antiqued. The amenities were awesome (Pecksniffs) and just everything about the room was classy. It is a very smart choice in SF compared to some of the other long standing Nob Hill establishments who have seemed to take a turn for the worse in recent years (Stanford Court, Fairmont, Huntington).A great business or adult getaway hotel.

<Author>wpack99
<Content>Flawless Booked a room using Priceline and was lucky enough to get the Omni San Francisco. The hotel pays attention to every detail, and I mean EVERY detail. Upon arrrival at the centrally located hotel, we were greeted by the doorman and others willing to help with baggage. There was a bit of a line at the check in desk and one of the bellmen quickly realized the need for additional resources. After advising those waiting he would secure additional help, he did just that. Soon the line was gone and everyone checked in quickly. The reservation was under my name but they allowed my wife to check in while I parked the car, simply asking that I return to the desk with my ID and credit card at some point durign our stay. Now that is service.When we arrived at the well appointed room, there was a hand written note from the housekeeper welcoming us. That is a first ever!That evening the room was turned down, chocolates were left and the television was tuned to a station that was entirely soothing music and beautiful scenes. Again, what an amazing touch.When we returned to the hotel on day 2, another hand written note from the housekeeper indicating she hoped we had a wonderful day, this time the note was personalized to us (vs. Dear Guest). We visited the bar as well and while the drinks were quite pricey ($15 for a martini) the atmosphere and service were perfect. I would highly recommend the Omni. Many others before me have given high ratings and I completely concurr. Excellent, absolutely excellent.

<Author>Ann06
<Content>Consistent Quality at the Omni Stayed here July 6-8. Though this hotel is ostensibly in the financial district it is very conveniently located for walking (at the base of Nob Hill) and to public transportation (cable car, for the patient) and BART (take it to the 16th street stop to go to Tartine Bakery at 18th  Guerrero). Pleasant walk to SF MOMA, AME Restaurant at the St. Regis Hotel (recommend) and Bong Su Restaurant. Hotel is representative of the attention to detail and quality that seem to be consistent with the Omni chain. Hotel staff are outgoing and pleasant. Check-in is effortlessly efficient. With Special Guest number (only sign up is required), there is free internet in the room. They also provide free beverages in the morning with this SG #. Opening window provides fresh air in the room, though the temperature control in the room is perfect. Nice bathroom amenities - lighted make-up mirror. Superior comfortable bed. Bathroom is a touch tiny. Hotel Manager informs me the hotel is planning a full renovation in 2008, but honestly, everything there is perfectly nice. Did not have an opportunity to use the work out facilities, but they are provided. Check out was automatic and accurate. Car waiting to provide airport transportation - nice not to have to wait for a taxi (and SF taxis make NYC taxis seem positively hygienic).

<Author>Chrisderfer
<Content>Great choice if you can get a great rate, otherwise maybe not Found a great deal for Memorial Day weekend....spent five nights here for $139/night (plus taxes).At this rate it was great and well worth my money, otherwise I don't think I'd come here again when rates reach $350+Lobby is fantastic, but as other reviews say, the glamour stops here. That doesn't mean the rest of the hotel is bad.Rooms: Standard rooms are small, but do include a nice size desk. Views from the room are just city block views, nothing exciting. Bathroom was very nice, with marble countertop and shower surround. Room staff left little well-wishing notes and Ghiradelli chocolate squares on the bed each night, a nice touch.Staff: Front desk staff was very helpful.Food: stay away from the breakfast...overpriced like most hotels of this type ($22 for continental breakfast? not for me.) I ordered room service from Bob's Chop House, which is apparently well known in SF as a good steak house. It was pretty good!Location: Easy walk to Ferry Building/Chinatown/Union Square. Beware, there's very little in the way of eating/shopping around the hotel since it's in the financial district....so if you find yourself in the mood for a quick eat, then you'll have to walk somewhere else or eat in the hotel.My next trip I'll probably stay in Union Square instead.

<Author>arthurtrejo
<Content>Another great stay at the Omni!!!!!! This was our fourth stay at the Omni and again was not disappointed. On this trip though we also stayed at the SF Marriot due to a buisness commitment. I have to say that we thought the SF Marriot was big, cold and impersonal as compared to the Omni. We loved the cozy feeling of the Omni---smaller hotel, quiet area on the weekend and not bad during the week, a cable car right out front, North Beach a short walk away, the compimentary beverages in the morning, the hot apple cider in the evenings and the fact that we saw the same staff everyday during our stay. They got to know us and were very helpful and attentive to our travel plans. Not so at the SF Marriot! The Deluxe room was well appointed but not luxurious. The bathroom was well light and had a make-up mirror as well (something my girlfriend wanted to point out). We also ate dinner at Bob's Steakhouse and I have to say that was one of the best steaks that I have eaten in a long while----be aware that the prices are not for those on a budget but if you want to splurge then it is well worth it. For the price [though the Select Guest program] the Omni is well worth it. FYI, we have stayed in a Deluxe room to a Signature room from the 6th to 17th floor. We preferred the deluxe room on the 6th floor as we actually enjoyed hearing the clangging of the cable car bell. If you prefer quit then get a room above the 8th floor. Note that the views from the Signature rooms could be blocked by nearby buildings. Overall the Omni has everything I have come to enjoy about it and is our hotel of choice in SF.

<Author>gardaconvert
<Content>Great Hotel Picked Omni from previous reviews... Some may say being on edge of financial district is quiet, well No! We experienced a Thursday, Friday and Saturday. Saturday was very quiet to get going as most local deli's etc within 10 min walk either do not open on Saturday or open later, say 10am which is fine. It is only 10 min walk from Ferry Building which has many cafes etc and markets at the weekend. Or just hop on cable car that goes past hotel and get off further up California Street to jump on cable car down to Union Square, 15 mins tops. Loads of places to eat there. The cable cars are great, get a $11 dollar all day ticket from hotal reception, valid for the cars and buses. Rooms are lovely, nice and big and great bathrooms, all marble, rooms have air con big TV , video games etc.We used as base to explore, Lombard street, G Gate bridge, Fishermans Wharf, Italian quarter, Coit Tower. Most is easily walkable but those hills can be pretty steep so the cable cars really do make it easy. One tip though.... it can be better to go the end of the line/terminus to get a car and join the queue as some are very busy and nobody gets off, hence you can wait at a stop and not get on at all. Busiest route is from the Market to Fishermansd Wharf via Hyde Street. This one passes over Lombard Street just by the 'crooked street' bit. Great fun standing on the side and leaning out.... which you are not supposed to do of course. We did have one evening meal in the Bob's Steakhouse, attached to hotel and one brealfast. Very good quality although a bit more expensive. Very very busy during the week with business people etc. The bar gets very crowded and noisy but in a nice happy, people enjoying themseleves sort of way.All the staff were very polite and extremely helpful, whatever the question is.

I would strongly recommend the omni to visitors. Staff very knowledgable on what's going on in town and recommended the best ways to get around. Great location in that it was in the downtown area but a couple of blocks away from all of the hustle and bustle on traffic and people. Would definitely stay there again.A great place to eat Chinese food is the R  G lounge on Kearny Street (two blocks behind the Omni) food was excellent and very affordable.

<Author>akula1957
<Content>Worked for our weekly vacation! We arrived and were surprised at how small the lobby was. Not a problem, just a suprise. Our room was fine for the three of us (48, 12, 10) with two double beds. The beds were very comfortable and big enough for the three of us. High ceilings. Nice bathroom. Service was very good. As a Omni Club Member we received free breakfast drinks at the door, free newspapers, and free afternoon brownies. A nice touch. As with many San Fran hotels, no pool. The location was good but not great. We were in the business district near Chinatown. We like walking so this was fine. (We almost picked the Argunaut but decided to not stay at the Wharf --- a good choice I think.) We never tried the hotel restaurant but enjoyed some hearby Chinese and LOVED the food and charm of the Italian neighborhood some blocks away (try The Stinking Rose and Cafe Greco). Walking to the Wharf was not too far for us. We took a taxi back rather than wait an hour for a cable car. (We luckily did not rent a car.) The Omni --- absolutely professional and no problems, but not spectacular. Would recommend if willing to walk around town.

<Author>NLProductn
<Content>Overrated -- Clean, Nice but definitely not outstanding. I am a little amazed at some of the reviews I have read here. Don't get me wrong this is a nice hotel but it doesn't warrant rave reviews, there are some problems.No wireless internet, I can't believe a hotel in the financial district doesn't have wireless internet. The front desk said we needed to pay 50 bucks to upgrade to a room with wireless internet. Huh? You have to be kidding me. The doormen (as all the reviews state here) were not (a) very friendly or (b) very helpful. I would suggest hospitality training.Don't be fooled by the candid pics above you probably won't get the room that shows a duvet (that isn't the room we got), this hotel still uses bedspreads -- very unsanitary (anytime you get a room witha bedspread throw it in the corner immediately) they're a haven for bacteria. Otherwise, the bed was clean and comfortable. The bath, amenities, and towels were adequate though not luxurious. This is nota 5 star hotel or comparative to the Four Seasons though it did remind me of a Ritz Carlton.Our first room smelled like smoke but we were relocated quickly, our bill was overcharged for a mini bar item but was corrected and our room service order was wrong but also was corrected after a call. Park at St. Mary's if you are staying on the weekend it 's 1/5 the price of the $45 parking rate and catty corner to the hotel. Plan on paying for parking, it is San Francisco. We probably would not do a car if we stayed in the city again, it's too hard with the steep slopes and we are used to driving a lot.The hotel was clean and the location is off the beaten path a bit although still relatively close to everything. The rooms were really clean and the young man at check in was nice and helpful. We got a great price for the weekend so the hotel was well worth our price it but I sure wouldn't want to pay full price for my stay. I would defintely move up to higher end. hotel if I were paying listed rates.There is no view, it was of another building but that is to be expected in the city.Here are some other tips: We had a cheap great lunch at the mexican restaurant communal dining Mijita at the Ferry Building and parking was only $5 with validation, we enjoyed walking around the Ferry Building marketplace but skipped the touristy Fisherman's Wharf. We took the ferry to Sausalito and that was great. We walked from the hotel to the Fodor reccommended L'Osteria del Forno for dinner - it'sless than a mile, go late or go early there is often a line but it iscash only, tiny but casual and we enjoyed the food. Great for the price.

<Author>Tobes01
<Content>Not bad at all I spent 8 nights at the Omni when attending a conference in San Francisco. The hotel's location is fantastic, bang in the middle of town without some of the grime associated with Union Square. The public areas and reception are clean and smart. The room was comfortable and quiet (courtyard rooms are quiet but with a view of the neighbouring office block), but very plain - nothing in there to denote it as special in any way. The service, however, was very good indeed - bright and attentive staff at every level from housekeeping to management. Room service food was fantastic, although for the most part I got take-aways from neighbouring Chinatown. I'll certainly use the Omni again.

<Author>DonnieDarker
<Content>Dont be put off by it not being on Market St or in Union Square A lot of reviews of this fabulous hotel say its in a quiet part of town (financial district) and coming from London you imagine this means that you'll need a taxi to get anwhere and the area will be quite eerie.WRONG.If you have a pair of legs and can walk you can be on Market St/Union Square in 5-10 minutes.I'm used to big busy cities and there is nothing worse than staying in the throbbing throng with all the tourists. For this reason the location of the Omni is a real bonus. Far from the madding crowd but no so far to be any kind of inconvenience.It is true that most of the guests seem to be there on business but its no problem. Dont eat there if you dont want to hear suits talk turkey. Go out and enjoy the many fanatsic restaurants in San Fran instead.TIPS:Join the SelectGuest programme (a kind of clubcard membership) for free in adavnce and then you get a free paper and drink delivered to your room every morning at a time you specify. You also get the option of ordering light breakfast items at an extremely reasonbale rate. (cream cheese toatsted bage was about $3 or 1.50).The gym is stocked with complimentary water and fresh(ish) fruit. 'Nuff said on that one!Free internet service in the lobby.If noise bothers you stay as high up as possible. (on the 5th you can hear the tram bells, on the 13th you can hear nothing).You can buy your MUNI passes from the fornt desk at their face value.If travelling without too much luggage do yourself a favour at SFO and use the BART rather than pay for a taxi. A jounrey on the BART is only $5.15 and the walk from Montgomery Station is less than 10 minutes. The BART was very safe and clean.ROOMS:Look nicer than they appear in the photos. They're quite dark which is why the photos dont do them justice. It's all very faux-Georgian but tastefully done. Bathrooms are classy too.Not enormous amounts of storage but enough. Avoid the mini-bar.SERVICE:Front-desk and doormen were superb. Extremely friendly and helpful. Nothing was too much trouble.Room service was extremely punctual with the selectguest drinks delivery. (you book a 15 minute slot and they there on the button every time).A Maitre D at Bobs steakhouse (attached to the Omni) was a bit stuffy but thats not their problem. Remember its mainly business people eating or using the bar there so I would avoid.LOCATION:You're in the business district but this does mean the area is well served by espresso bars, jamba juice and diners for workers. Also, a tram stops outide the hotel which is handy.You can walk most places very easily or use your MUNI pass for the transport.

<Author>Gemma'smum
<Content>Perfect location for Family vist to Chinese New Year We were thoroughly pleased with our stay at the Omni. We had adjoining rooms (a King and a double) and were assistd at every turn by Omnii staff. We have stayed in more than a dozen hotels in S.F. (St. Francis, the Palace, the Milano, Hyatts, Mariott, Sir Francis Drake, Kensington Park etc.) over the years and this was definately among the best. Many hotels will have nice lobbies, but have very ordinary rooms . The Omni had beautifully furnished luxurious rooms with every imaginable amenitiy. I would recommend it to anyone. As San Francisco is developing more and more to the east of Union Square, restaurants, shopping and attractions are near the Financial District location of the Omni. Plus, the California Cable Car line is right outside. We were in S.F. for the Chinese New Year Parade (a block away), Prom Dress Shopping, (5 min walk) and to attend an event at MoMA (10 minute walk). Nearby Belden Place offers some of San Franciscos best restaurants and a truly european bistro experience, that is entirely family friendly. We had dinner at Brindisi. Make reservations for weekends at any S.F. restaurant.. The hotel valet parking is $45 , high even for San Francisco. However, around the corner on Kearny is a 24 hour city parking lot with security. A bargain. If you join the Omni's club before your stay, you also get real pampering including morning coffee delivered to your door with the paper and free internet. We loved it!

<Author>JRSanchez
<Content>Great Service, Great Hotel, Great Stay! We booked the Omni based on two factors: price for 2 rooms as given through Expedia and also reviews from Trip Advisor. This was a getaway weekend for me, 2 adult sisters, and our Mom to celebrate Mom's birthday.BACKGROUND: Each member of our gang is a very seasoned world traveler, and we have stayed in every type of accommodation around the world from the St. Regis and Four Seasons to camping in a tent on Kuaui, with many a hostel experience thrown in for good measure. We are also all veteran San Francisco travelers, with one sister having lived in the city at one time. We have stayed all over the city in all types of properties (large and small, cheap and luxury) and we ALL AGREE: The Omni gets our unanimous vote as our new San Francisco home away from home!!! From check in to check out, everything was smooth and wonderful and the staff, from the front desk to the housekeeping staff, could not have been nicer or more accommodating.FRONT DESK: We checked in on Friday and arrived quite early (10.30 a.m.) expecting to have to store our luggage until later in the day. Surprise! Two rooms were ready and waiting. However, upon getting up to the rooms, we discovered that we had one room with 2 doubles and one with 1 king. We wanted to have two rooms, both with doubles, connecting if possible. One call to the front desk, a thorough search of the computer, and VOILA: just what we wanted. Not only that, but the bellman brought up the keys to the new rooms so we did not even have to go downstairs again.The bellman made sure to get all of our luggage sorted out, gave us a run-down on the hotel's services, put himself at our complete disposal, and was just a friendly as he could be. It is clearly obvious that whomever is providing the customer service training for the staff is to be highly commended: not ONCE did we ever receive anything less that a gracious smile, a hello, and an offer to assist. We also requested a VERY late check out (3 p.m.) and were accommodated without a hitch.AMENITIES: the hotel has a great fitness center with lots of cardio options, headphones for the plasma screen individual TV units, and free bottled water. Also has reciprocity for the full scale fitness club located across the street.Guest rooms have blow dryers, good lighting in the bathroom and elsewhere in the room, full tub with shower, nice toiletries, robes, and an in-room safe. Lighted closet with lots of hangers, and minibar too. There is FREE high-speed interenet access in the room (hard wired) as well as a business center that offers free internet if you did not bring your own laptop. They will also print free pages for you if needed.....Also: the WINDOWS in the rooms open to allow for fresh air ventilation! We love this! The heating / ac unit if very quiet and powerful too. With the windows open there is some street noise (even at higher levels) but we didn't mind.BEDS: comfy, comfy, firm and soft at the same time, duvet comforters, with great pillow choice. Pillows are an issue with me  I usually travel everywhere with my own to avoid vacation-ruining neck pain, but I left mine behind in the interest of packing light. I was not disappointed!THE AREA: The location of the hotel is downtown near the financial center, near the end of the California cable car line and the Montgomery Street BART station. It is very convenient if you are doing business in the area during the week, and much quieter if you stay on the weeknd as we did. Many of the close-by cafes and coffee shops close over the weekend. However, there are PLENTY within easy walking distance (within 10 block radius) that are open all weekend. You can walk to Union Square in one direction and the Ferry Plaza Marketplace in the other direction and be in either location within 10 minutes. Also: this is a SAFE walk and you will not pass by too many homeless (a problem in any large city, sadly).TRANSPORTATION: If you are uncomfortable or unable to walk, the hotel has Guest Cars (town cars) that will happily take you anywhere in the city you would like to go (or back to the airport when you leave, crying). The doorman will let you know the cost BEFORE you get in the car, and the price is comprable to taking a cab, and much cleaner. The front desk staff can direct you to and make reservations for you at any of the terrific SF restaurants. EATING: This is a city that runs on it's stomach. For morning (or afternoon) lattes  cappucino, we would recommend a stroll through North Beach with a stop at CAFFE PUCCINI near the corner of Columbus  Vallejo (next to Tratoria Pinnochio). Also, MOLINARI'S ITALIAN DELI (on Columbus) for sandwiches  the Salami. They make their own  are famous for it. For dinner  lunch, we would happily recommend BOULEVARD (great location, fantastic food  service, very pricey) as well as YANK SING (dim sum, extended lunch hours only, including weekends, great food, traditional cart serving, moderately pricey depending on your appetite, delicious).In addition, if you go over the weekend, you MUST go to the Saturday Morning Farmer's Market at the Ferry Plaza. This is not to be missed, and go hungry, as you will be able to eat everything from pastries to tamales, with coffee bars, cheese, fruits  veggies. Definitely worth a stop an a beautiful weekend to get your picnic fixins on your way out to Angel Island, Alcatraz, or the Marina District or Golden Gate Park.Whew! Thanks for reading through to the end. I hope that if you stay at the Omni, you will be as pleased as we were. Have FUN!

<Author>Jezza1
<Content>Great hotel, good location We stayed at the Omni for three nights in February. A very high quality hotel, located 5-10 mins cab ride from Union Square. Although its in the business district, and so the local area is really quiet / closed at the weekend, there are some really nice restaurants about 2 mins walk away - just ask at reception for recommendations. Rooms are lovely - very clean, spacious, big bed, very quiet etc.. Some great touches like free internet access in Business Centre, free hot chocolate by the lifts - the mark of a really customer orientated hotel.The only downside is the poor choice of healthy meals in the bar - but as there are some nice restaurants nearby not really a major problem.Much better value for a weekend stay than the hotels in the tourist traps at Fisherman's Wharf. Another TripAdvisor winner!

<Content>Lovely Hotel I've stayed at this hotel before, and there was a reason I returned. This time the valet guys weren't as attentive, and one of the guys actually slammed the door on me to help another guest, a total over sight on his part, but nonetheless, a little annoying since my roller bag got caught in the door, and I almost fell. For lunch they have a $11 minimum per person. Another top restaurant is Aqua, walking distance, but make reservations early, and you are looking at a $75/pp prefixe menu, but this place is a rage right now.

<Author>m0thily
<Content>Beautiful, luxury, no complaints What a beautiful hotel... It was in the perfect location (4 blocks from BART, short walk from Union Square and Westfield/SF Centre), but reasonably quiet and not crowded with the usual tourist throngs.The check-in process was seamless and cheerful, and the door staff was pleasant and helpful.If you're thoughtless enough to have brought a car, as I did, be warned that valet parking is expensive (we were charged $45/day plus city tax) and the nearby garages were full on a weekday afternoon. To their credit, the staffers were upfront about the price and didn't charge us extra, even though we left the car there for more than 24 hours.The room was well-appointed and luxurious, with a nice, clean bathroom, bathrobes and linens. One minor complaint we had was the quality of the bedding... my mattress was sagging on one side, and my friend's pillows were very lumpy. The mattresses and pillows seemed to be in need of replacement, in general. But it wasn't bad enough for us to switch rooms or ask for new pillows. We might've been upset if we had to pay a lot (say $250+/night) for our stay, but we got a deal, so... just something to keep in mind if you're expecting pure perfection and paying rack rates. In all, we were very happy with the hotel and would definitely recommend it and stay here again if the price is right next time.

<Author>101travelers
<Content>Omni style and service! We spent two nights at the Omni after Christmas. Having stayed at the Omni San Diego, I was curious to see if the San Francisco hotel was deserving of its #1 rating by TripAdvisor reviewers. I booked directly through the Omni website and the $199 Park and Play offer included parking and a superior room. Having paid approximately $48 a night for parking at a hotel in the Union Square area, this seemed a great deal. As a Select Guest, registration info is on file and so you basically walk up to the desk and receive your room card. I had requested and received a front-facing (California St) room on a high floor. The lobby area was beautifully decorated and complimentary hot cider and cookies were available. The bed was extremely comfortable, as was the large armchair with ottoman. The room is tastefully decorated with a large work desk, many lamps, Bose radio and armoire with television/coffee service/mini-bar and large drawers for clothing. The large closet has a safe and bathrobes. The bathroom was large with a huge shower/tub with great water pressure. Large make-up mirror, too. As mentioned, Select Guest program will get you beverages and a newspaper, delivered at the time you designate. Some breakfast items offered to SGs at $2-4 such as bagels, muffins or breakfast burrito. Great prices! More extensive menu available through room service. This is one of the few hotels that delivers a large carafe of coffee if that is your selected beverage. Bagels come toasted, wrapped in a cloth napkin and with cream cheese and an assortment of fruit preserves. The steakhouse restaurant has very good food- a variety of soups, salads and sandwiches were on lunch menu. Prices a bit high but not out of line for SF restaurants. Staff very attentive. Hotel very quiet but the city, and Financial District in particular, have a low occupancy rate during the holiday period. This hotel is an excellent choice for business travellers.

<Author>Daisy Larchmont
<Content>The Omni Gets It Right My 3-day New Year's getaway at the Omni SF reconfirmed my committment to this luxury hotel chain. I booked a 2-night stay via Expedia at an incredible rate, about $120 per night. I normally opt for affordablility over luxury, but sometimes you just want to be pampered and are willing to pay a little bit more. For those occasions, you can't go wrong with Omni. They understand the what a true luxury hotel experience is all about. At Omni, the customer is always right, and the customer's needs always come first. Case in point- my room key did not work upon check-in (they had given me a room that was still occupied, oops), and when I returned to the front desk, they upgraded me to a 2-room corner suite for my trouble, apologizing all the while. This was followed up with a personal note of apology from the front desk manager the next morning - and a fresh fruit basket in the afternoon, again gratis. The suite (room 920) was gorgeous, with a sitting room, 2 flat-screen TVs, and a DVD player. One of the nice things about staying in the Financial District is that it's very quiet at night - no sirens, ambulances, etc.I joined the Select Guest program several years ago. As others have noted, I highly recommended joining for the free perks. I enjoyed the complimentary beverages (choice of 2 - try the coffee and hot chocolate together!) and morning paper, and was pleasantly suprised to find that this Omni also offered Select Guests a range of reduced-price breakfast items along with the complimentary morning beverages. For $3.75 each, we ordered the breakfast burritos, which were hefty and delicious, served with fresh salsa. Imagine - a delicious room-service breakfast in SF for under $5! I stll can't quite understand how this place made money off my stay....I guess it all averages out in their favor. Stay here, you'll be glad you did.

<Content>Excellent Hotel - Highly Recommended As usual, I left everything to the last minute and booked this hotel the day before I was due to stay. I got a really good deal on it (about 100 per night), I was a bit worried about the quality of the hotel, but it was the only decent one available. I was 100% pleased with this hotel. <Content>Most pleasant hotel stay in years! I visit SF often and, in the past, have stayed in inexpensive hotels on the premise that it's just a place to sleep. I've always felt that I'd rather spend my hard-earned money on something more important than a hotel room (e.g. a nice meal or a theater ticket).It was Christmas night and the Omni offered a deal that was too exceptional to pass up. For about double the price of the lowest category El Dumpo (including tax), I decided to treat myself to the Omni.The glowing reviews are well-deserved. The hotel, rooms and staff lacked NOTHING. Everything was sparkling clean, the service was friendly and efficient. Replacement batteries for a remote control arrived within 15 minutes of my call. The room-service breakfast arrived punctally and hot. Free internet in the lobby and a daily newspaper on your door. Gorgeous bath with everything you could want (including cotton balls, Qtips and sewing kit). Iron, umbrella and robes in the closet. Turn-down service. All in-room electronic amenities. Get the picture? Absolutely no negatives! As long as I can get a weekend rate near the one I just enjoyed, I'll never stay elsewhere again in SF.

<Author>evening
<Content>I used to love the Omni - but that's all over now! If I hadnt stayed at the Omni San Francisco in the past, or had such wonderful service at the Marriott Baltimore Waterfront last week, maybe I'd feel differently about my recent stay at the Omni, but I will now find a new hotel for future visits to San Francisco.Yes, incidents are usually isolated, but I had a problem with the doormen upon arrival and departure (different guys), so feel comfortable stating that the service has deteriorated greatly. Not to mention - the pillows sucked! The so called feather pillow must have been stuffed with ping pong balls!I am not some princessy woman, but it is ridiculous that a woman travelling alone should be expected to remove her own huge bag from the back of a cab when arriving at a hotel of the caliber of the Omni. Especially while the doorman stands there commenting how the driver isnt a nice guy for not removing the bag. Then the bellman standing at the bottom of the steps watches you carry your bags down them instead of asking to help (or pointing out that the ramp to nowhere does eventually lead to the lobby).But the worst - was when I asked the doorman to call a cab for my return trip to the airport and he suggested I take the house car for a couple of dollars more. Trusting the doorman at an Omni wouldnt scam me, I jumped in the house car. As soon as the driver told me the fee, I had to have him bring me back to the hotel! The cab from/to the airport was $27. The house car is $45. How would I justify that to my company??? I have to state the maid - Tina - was wonderful.I used to stay ONLY at Omnis when traveling to cities that had them - until 2004 when the receptionist at the New Orleans Omni made an innapropriate political comment when she transfered my call to voicemail. This return trip to the San Francisco Omni was probation. They failed miserably and I am done with the Omni.

<Author>Gibso
<Content>Great Hotel ,perfect location I've just returned from a 5 night stay at the Omni and really if you want an excellent hotel in a great location this has to be your choice. The rooms are of a good size with large bathrooms and a walk in shower, i had a premier room which was an upgrade from a deluxe room which i paid for ,to recieve this uprade sign up to Omni Hotels signature program and you will recieve this for free as well as other benefits such as late check out. As all the other reviews state the staff are excellent, i travelled with my 2 year old daughter and all the staff made a fuss of her. As far as location goes to me this is in the best location in the city union square shopping is 10 mins walk in one direction and fishermans walf 20 mins in the other and north beach and chinatown on your doorstep, although there are plenty of buses ,cable cars and taxis if you want to take it easy. I booked with hotel connect a uk website which were 400 cheaper on my booking than any other website. Room service is expensive but breakfast in you room is nice, go on treat yourself ,your on holiday.

<Author>lanh
<Content>If you have kids, don't stay anywhere else. We stayed for 4 days over the Labor Day holiday weekend, and we had an excellent experience.I booked directly through the hotel website so that I could make a special request for a crib, as well as give them my Select Guest number. When we arrived, the crib was already set up and waiting in our room for us, together with a handwritten note addressing us by name and welcoming us to the Omni. There were a few baby toiletries tucked away into the crib, as well.I do recommend applying for a Select Guest number (you can do this online) beforehand, as it entitles you to a few amenities including late checkout. If you do it well ahead of time, I think they might send you a 50% off coupon and free room upgrade, too -- this happens either a few weeks after you apply or else a little after your first stay. (I'm not sure which, as we registered and made our booking at the last minute.) You can also buy these coupons on ebay, and they're fully transferable. (It says so on the coupon.) This might be very worth your while if you're staying for several days. If we had known about the Omni ahead of time, we would have planned ahead to get this.You also get free morning beverages in your room for all the people staying -- 2 beverages per person. We had 2 adults and our two children (ages 3 and 1) and got coffee for 4 and orange juice for 4 every morning, for example. You need to remember to put the little Select Guest hang tag, which they give you with your key, on your door ahead of time to receive this. You will also get a morning paper (you choose which paper), as well as a scone-like cookies and milk every evening with your turndown service.The room is fairly standard for a hotel room but quite comfortable. The bed linens are good quality, and the bathrooms are very roomy and marble. Everything is spotless. I was surprised the towels were not softer -- they're thin and not very comfortable, but they're serviceable and clean. We did request a room upgrade if they were available, and I was disappointed not to be upgraded for free (they said I could pay an extra $100 for a suite), but I certainly wasn't entitled to this so that's fine. That is the only disappointment of our Omni experience, and it is extremely minor.We had two small children with us, and the Omni is fantastic for families with children. The kids got a great goodie bag with crayons, activity books, playing cards, and even a small digital clock that they could hang from their coats or suitcases. My 3 year old was delighted with the bag, and she can be a tough customer! You can also request a Kids' Suitcase from the front desk, and this is literally a small rolling suitcase full of things like an Etch a Sketch, electronic games device, card games like Go Fish and Old Maid, and several classic books (Goodnight Moon, some kids' chapter books). We had a babysitter coming in one night (not associated with the hotel) and found this suitcase extremely handy for the night we were away from the kids. You also are given free kids' straw cups that you can take down to the restaurant to have filled for free. We filled up with milk for the kids every morning and night, and they were fast and gracious about it even though we weren't staying for dinner or breakfast or anything.All the service people were wonderful (with the exception of one woman who was just a bit brusque working the front desk at night. She wasn't rude though, just minimally helpful). The doormen were great. Bell service was instantaneous when we called for it. I had to ask for housekeeping to clean up a spill once, and they came to the room within minutes. The doormen refused our tips.Oh -- and I was wary because I had read that the parking fee was $45 a day. When we pulled up, the valets asked us whether we preferred the $45 hotel parking or wanted to park ourselves at the garage a half-block away, for $7. There was no pressure at all, and they were not at all condescending. You can park at St Mary's Garage at the intersection of California and Kearny for $7 per in/out on holidays and weekends. It's very convenient, and the hotel told us about it themselves.

<Author>philipellis
<Content>faultless service with a smile my wife and I stayed at the SF Omni for 4 nights early august. on arrival, we were a little deflated because we had travelled from one of the uber-casino-hotels in vegas, but (back on planet earth after vegas!) the omni quickly won us over with its always pleasant staff, its cleanliness and (in our opinion and not withstanding other comments) its location.our room was on the 17th floor, with OK views. the room itself was fairly standard, of average size with an acceptable ensuite. the main factor in any room is its cleanliness, and here the omni was perfect: clean bedding, towels and surfaces made us warm to the hotel immediately.check in staff were pleasant and efficient, and full of tips about where to go and how to get there. its only a 7 buck taxi down to the piers, and a quick cable car ride to union square. its also possible to walk back to the hotel from union square because much of the walk is downhill; its an arduous journey the other way!china town is literally on the hotel doorstep; step out, turn right, walk one block and you're there.san francisco is great and a visit to alcatraz a must - although you have to pre-book - don't wait 'til you arrive.we got a town car from the hotel back to the airport - the same price as the taxi on the inward leg but much comfier and a nicer drive. maybe the hotel could send a car to the airport to pick you up - its certainly worth enquiring 'cos some of the SF cab drivers are not the best we've ever met!10/10 for the omni - it deserves its high standing on trip advisor.

<Author>Maryandfamily
<Content>Outstanding in every way My husband, two middle school aged children and I had the great pleasure of staying at the Omni San Francisco for four evenings (two on the front end of our drive North on Highway 1 and two on the back end of the drive before our return home). This is simply a gem in the heart of San Francisco. One of the cable car lines runs directly in front of the hotel. Our room was perfect. Comfortable, all of the amenities, quiet. Housekeeping is friendly, gracious and respectful of guests' privacy. We even had complimentary milk and pastries at bedtime. Every staff member we encountered was well-trained, genuinely concerned about our comfort, always offering a smile, exceptionally polite. We'd be remiss if we didn't single out 'Dorian', a bellhop who took considerable time with us to offer kid-friendly (and parent-friendly) touring suggestions. He didn't steer us wrong. We took his advice and road bicycles across the Golden Gate Bridge. We went to the Monet exhibit. 'Dorian' greeted us as if we were old friends. When we encountered a glitch with our rental car (it didn't arrive as scheduled for our drive North), 'Joey' arranged for a complimentary (delicious!) breakfast in the hotel restaurant while we waited. And, as if that wasn't enough, he presented us with a cooler filled to the brim with juices, water, and soft drinks for the drive. Now that's first-class! The only thing I would add to this wonderful experience is a gift shop (there isn't one). The nearby Walgreen's closes at 7pm and a place to shop for a few snacks (other than the room mini-bar), and even a San Francisco souvenir would be a delightful addition.

<Author>kd2006
<Content>Wonderful but not a good location The reviews on here were so good, I had to see for myself. It really is as great as everyone says! The beds are so comfortable and the rooms are decorated beautifully. The bathroom is large and they even give you an iron, a scale, q-tips, and cotton swabs! The maid even leaves a little note welcoming you.It was so wonderful having a scone with milk sitting there waiting for us before we went to bed. The service is wonderful.However, there is a downside - the location.The Omni is located in the Financial District and it is very difficult to find places to eat (unless you want Chinese food). It was Sunday night at 7PM and we walked around for at least an hour looking for a place to eat. We searched and even the nearby McDonald's was closed. We finally asked the person at the front desk who showed us where somewhere to eat was but it was closed.The Omni is also not close to many of the sights but the Cable Car stops right in front of the hotel.The food at Bob's had big, bland, and overpriced portions (in my opinion). Four shrimps with the shrimp cocktail for $15. Parking is $45 a night but you can come and go as you please.

<Author>T-bar
<Content>Great Staff Here's just an example of Omni's service: Two of us stayed at the Omni to end a weeklong trip in northern CA. We arrived in a rental car on a busy, rainy Friday afternoon. Our plan was to check in, then drop the car at the airport and return on the train. Bags were unloaded and check-in was smooth and painless. On the way to the airport we realized that neither of us told the bell staff our names or what room we were staying in -- we both thought the other had done it. Our bags were on a cart in the lobby. I figured a 1-star hotel would leave the bags where they were, a 3-star hotel would put them aside somewhere and leave us to get them when we returned (this would have been fine in my book), and a 5-star hotel would check the bag tags, check with the front desk for our names, and have them in the room by the time we returned. Of course the bags were waiting for us in the room, and it was a great worry-free start to a wonderful weekend at the Omni.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice hotel - not the best location for leisure Stayed at the Omni San Fran from a Friday until a Tuesday for leisure. It's very close to Chinatown, but there are hotels that are closer to Union Square that are just as nice if not nicer. I stayed at the JW Marriott for a night a couple of weeks later and found that to be a better location that was closer to shopping and restaurants. There is really nothing right next to the Omni. Don't get me wrong, the Omni isn't super far from anything, but it's not just a block walk. It's a short taxi ride to North Beach. I got a pretty good deal on the hotel (average $200 a night with the discount heavily on the weekend portion of the trip), which is probably because of its location. San Fran is made for walking, and with the Omni, you will. It's probably considered more of a business hotel than I knew it to be when I booked the trip. Staff was friendly, although not too much interaction. They seemed adequately staffed regardless of the volume of people in the lobby. I liked the free computer access. The room was just OK and not spectacular. Nice big king bed, but the carpet was kind of dirty. Bathroom was good too, but, again, not spectacular. I would stay at JW marriott over the Omni on my next trip.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fabulous Hotel!! My boyfriend and I stayed at the Omni San Francisco May 27-31st. We had a wonderful stay and I could not recommend this hotel more highly! The room was beautiful and spacious and extermely clean. I have never stayed in hotel room more spotless than this one. Even our spare toilet paper roll was wrapped in pink ribbon!!The doormen were always at the ready to open the door or help if you had any questions. The service here is impeccable. We had a problem with our toilet one night and the service person arrived in less than 5 minutes and had it fixed immediately. The location of this hotel is perfect. It's away from the hustle and bustle of Fisherman's wharf and the seedier Union Square. We rented a car and were glad we did as the lines for the cable cars were extremely long-being a holiday weekend. To avoid paying for parking, if you are there on a weekend and have the patience to find a spot, you can park overnight on the street if your meter isn't chargeable on weekends. Otherwise, if you park one block up at the St Mary's garage, it's about $20.00---which beats the $50 you have to pay to park at the hotel.I recommend this property to anyone who is going to San Francisco. EXCELLENT hotel and will absolutely stay here again!!

<Content>Loved the Omni Hi, my husband and I stayed at the Omni overnight in mid-May. Our room was lovely and clean. Will most definitely stay there on our next visit to beautiful San Franciso. We were there on a Saturday evening, and unlike another reviewer, we did not even notice that the vicinity surrounding the Omni was particularly quiet. We are in our late 50's and walked all through Chinatown to North Beach for dinnner and back again, returning after 11pm. Area felt very safe and we enjoyed the walk after our dinner. All of the staff we dealt with, front desk, doormen and parking valets were very courteous and efficient. The parking charge for your vehicle could make you weep though. We know better than to take a car into San Francisco but were forced to do so by circumstances. We were given a late check-out with absolutely no hesitation and the bellman kept our luggage for a few hours after that. We were so very pleased with our stay at the Omni. I will add that this was our fourth time in San Francisco and I think we enjoyed it even more this time.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Memorial Day Getaway! Spent the Memorial Day holiday weekend in San Fran with my girlfriend  decided to stay at the Omni purely off of the reviews from this site. I must say this service really does work, we were not disappointed. Flew into SFO on Friday night  requested a town car to pick us up curbside thru the hotel. The cost was a flat rate of $60 door to door  they can charge it to your room. You could pay around $45 for the same ride with a cab but then again your pulling up to the Omni, not the Holiday Inn. First thing we noticed upon arrival was the professionalism  friendliness that you would expect from the doormen to the luggage attendant. For a relatively small hotel it has a grand entrance with brass  marble appointments all of which can be seen thru their website. Once we checked in we arrived at our rooms accompanied by our luggage attendant who pointed out all the features of our room. I chose the premier room which had a little extra room compared to the delux rooms they offered. The bathroom was covered in marble  had all the creature comforts of home including a great blowdryer, soft robes, lotions, sewing kit, etc. The room was very clean  the bed was soft  warm. The fitness room was great  offered bottled water for free as well as starbucks coffee, just go early because they run out quick. DO NOT rent a car if you plan on exploring the surrounding neighborhoods, parking there is rediculous  could probably ruin your trip. Everything you ever needed to see in SF is within walking distance. All in all the hotel was great  I would highly recommend it to anyone who wants to plan a romantic getaway.

<Content>Childrens fantasy suite was excellent Spent 4 nights here with wife and 2 small children. It was delightful.We stayed in the kids fantasy suite. This suite (only 1 in the hotel) is not bookable on the internet, only by phone and consists of 2 adjoining bedrooms one of which has had all adult furniture removed and replaced with kids furniture.. bunk beds, soft toys, games, bean bags, posters etc. It was the perfect place to be after 11 hour flight from London. The children loved it. The adult room was very nicely decorated and comfortable. The staff also provided goodie bags for the children on arrival which was a nice touch. The location was good also. 10 minutes walk from downtown shopping areas, 5 minutes from Chinatown and convenient for all the trams. <Author>Phunky
<Content>Absolutely Beautiful Room I stayed at The San Francisco Omni in January during a business trip. I had heard that this chain was good, but my expectations were not high enough. This place was very nice, and because I was a Select Guest (SG) they upgraded my room to a bigger one. Very nice!Positives: Location right on California Street provides a short trolley ride up to Chinatown. Actually, you can walk to just about anywhere in SF, so ride the $5 trolley only if you have to. The room was great, and the bed was incredibly comfortable. The bathroom was huge (upgraded room), and they had free high-speed internet.Negatives: The staff was a bit pretentious. I work in IT and at the time I didn't have to wear a suit and tie like most of the business travellers there. The bellmen would open the door for anyone walking up, but they would just look me up and down like I didn't belong. I learned to take the side entrance on Montgomery so I could skip that whole uncomfortable feeling.The onsite steakhouse is average at best. The glazed carrot that they serve with every steak oozed it's glazing onto my steak. Not the best taste combo.For weekend travel you might find a better place to stay. The Omni is in the Financial District, so a lot of stuff is closed during the weekend. However, you can walk anywhere, even, but it might take a little bit longer to get to the other parts of the city.I really enjoyed my stay at The San Francisco Omni, and I would stay there again. It was a terrific room.

<Author>Nalrud
<Content>Nice hotel remote location unless in town on business... Omni Hotel in San Fran... is beautiful however it is a bit remote if you are not in town for business. During weekdays you are in a bustling business district full of places to eat, have coffee or people watch however during evening hours and especially on weekends the area is quite empty. On Sunday morning we stopped by 3 different starbucks stores that are located in the 2 blocks radius of the hotel until we found one (4th) that was open and that one obviously had a line outside...The staff at the hotel is very accommodating. The hotel lobby is stunning and the room was lovely, a walk-in closet was a plus. No complains about large windows or spaciousness of the room however the bath while quite nice and clean, lacked a hand shower or a flexible enough top shower where you can point it to the wall when needed. A squeaky pocket door separating the room from the bath was not the best either but that is an easy fix (call the staff resolved in minutes)...Overall, very nice hotel however if you are in San Fran... for pleasure pick a different area...

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Exceeded my expectations This hotel was excellent. The location was great! You literally are right in between Chinatown and fisherman wharf! There is a trolley stop right in front of the hotel and a subway across the street. The service was wonderful and the rooms overwhelmingly exceeded my expectations. There room service is ok, but like any hotel they way overcharge you for food and water. There is a Walgreen a block down Montgomery street and you can get a six pack of water or one large water for about 1/3 the price. The concierge was excellent and very helpful. Defiantly buy the Muni pass they offer it WILL save you a lot of money! My husband and I are just average people and we thought that since this was the Omni that maybe we would be treated poorly but not at all. We received excellent treatment. <Author>Psboston7
<Content>Absolutely WORTH every cent! the very best hotel EVER! We made reservations for this hotel through priceline but I must say after our stay I think I will never stay at any OTHER hotel when I am in San Francisco. Being that my background is hospitality and hotels in particular, (used to work for and open Marriott Hotels, Starwoods, Sheratons and Forte) when I say this it the VERY BEST HOTEL that I have stayed in EVER that is saying a lot.Customer service was ABOVE AND BEYOND Fantastic. To clarify yes the valet is $45.00 (in line with city parking) however we parked at the Chinese Catholic Center on Jackson st  it was $24 not far from the hotel either. The location is close to Chinatown  North Beach, although it sits in the heart of the Financial District the cable car stop is right outside your door so really no need to rent a car unless you have to also the Front Desk sells all day muni passes for $11 which is a really good buy if you will be traveling the city it is good for the cable cars as well as the buses. The rooms are spacious, nicely appointed the amenities are luxurious, linens are DIVINE, housekeeping associates were friendly and consistently available. Room service was expensive but the late night menu was delicious and they even allowed us to order desserts from the regular menu (although it was pass the cut-off time)Front desk associates were attentive  VERY, VERY helpful (Carmen in particular) complimentary in room wireless internet, complimentary business center with internet access, do yourself a favor  do as a reviewer before me recommended  sign up for the omni hotel frequent guest program the check out is at 5:00pm  every morning they bring up complimentary newspapers and beverages of your choice they do this also in the evening with milk  cookies (although I think this was done becuase we traveled with teenagers) Saying all this I was very impressed with the Omni Hotel and think that perhaps there is hope for our Hospitality industry in the Customer Servicedepartment since the past 6 years I have seen a decline this hotel has renewed my inspiration for our Industry. WELL DONE!Respectfully Reviewed

<Author>tdandmd
<Content>Great hotel that's just a little out of the way This is a great smaller hotel that is in the Financial District and therefore quite a bit quieter than the usual Union Square, Fisherman Wharf, etc. locations yet super close to all that and more.The hotel is a converted/refurbished old business building and you would expect it to be dark and cramped but the common areas were beautiful and the room was decent size and very clean and modern. The bathroom was nice with great soaps and things. The room also came with robes, a safe and umbrella.As I noted, after about 6:00 the Financial District is pretty much deserted, but you are only about two blocks from China Town, four blocks from Union Square (by way of some great shopping streets in and of themselves), a couple blocks from Fisherman's Wharf, a couple blocks to North Beach, a couple blocks to the Metreon, a couple blocks to the new Ferry Building. Plus, you have a great bar/restaurant right in your own hotel and the Carnelian Room (for the view) across the street in the Bank of America Building. And on top of all that, the cable car goes right by the front door so you can hop on and be on Nob Hill in no time without hiking up the hills yourself.The only negative that we have to say is that the parking was $45, which is just ridiculous. If we hadn't been so pressed for time when we arrived late, we would have parked it ourselves up the street at the St. Mary's garage for $20 (which is what you know the hotel is probably doing.) Of course, the good part was that we got this through Priceline (I had a good idea this was the hotel I was bidding on so I went for it) for $75 for a Saturday night at Christmas shopping time.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Highly recommend the Omni My husband and I stayed at the Omni for 5 nights over the Christmas weekend. We had a blast in SF, and can attribute a lot of that to the great hotel we selected. The location was perfect. Comfortable walking distance to Union Square, Chinatown, the Embarcadero and Little Italy. We also walked back and forth to Fisherman's Wharf several times along Columbus Ave and other routes; it gave us a good opporutunity to explore different areas. Don't be intimidated to walk up some of the hills; you'll be sure to get a great view once you get to the top. Some more tips about staying at the Omni: 1.) Don't drive or rent a car, you won't need one. Bring good walking shoes and you'll be able to walk everywhere. We especially enjoyed walking to Chinatown for lunch (for really good, cheap Dim Sum, check out House of Dim Sum) and to Columbus Ave in Little Italy for a mid-afternoon espresso at Cafe Puccini. Good for just relaxing after a day of sight-seeing. 2.) If you fly into SFO, just take BART to the Montgomery Street station. The Omni is a 10 minute walk from the Montgomery Street BART station and it only costs $5. 3.) Sign up for the select guest program through the Omni website. You get free drinks every morning, which doesn't sound like a big deal, but it was a great way to start out the morning - pot of coffee and OJ before you even leave the room. You also get turndown service which is great; the maid left us cute little notes every day 4.) If you like Jazz, definitely check out Jazz at Pearl's, just a short walk from the Omni.

<Author>SLOJJ
<Content>Excellent Hotel in San Francisco My husband and I just returned from a Saturday night stay at the Omni with our two year old and were extremely pleased with the hotel. We have stayed in several hotels in San Francisco and our room at the Omni was by far the largest. We used Priceline and got a rate of $80, then upgraded at check-in for another $25 to a very spacious room that worked well for the three of us. I was really surprised to get such a reasonable rate in the middle of the holiday season in the city. We followed the advice of a reviewer and skipped the $53 valet parking fee by parking one block up at the St. Mary's Square garage (on Kearney) for $6.50 for 24 hours. Hard to believe you can park anywhere in San Francisco for $6.50, but parking on the weekend in the Financial District was a great tip. The other tip we used was to enroll in Omni's preferred guest program on their website before we checked in. Not only did it get us complementary beverages and a paper in the morning, but it allowed us to check out anytime before 5 p.m. the next day. We were able to do some shopping (and eat dim sum in Chinatown) on Sunday morning, then return to our hotel room and let our toddler take a nap before leaving town. The staff were very friendly and gave our little one a welcome bag of goodies when we checked in, and we were pleased to see other children at the hotel, although the rooms were very quiet. The Omni is ideally located within walking distance of Chinatown, Union Square, and the Ferry Building. We'll definitely stay there again.

<Author>TP1234
<Content>We had high expectations, and we were not disappointed My family spent five nights at the Omni San Francisco during the Thanksgiving week, and we had a wonderful time. I have been in many hotels in San Francisco before but never at the Omni. Ie heard great things about it from my colleagues and have read consistent, good reviews on the web. I decided to give a try for our family vacation, considering someone in the family is usually picky about hotels.The room was very clean and well equipped with everything, including bathrobes. The marble bathtub was sparkling and the bed was very comfy. The entire staff was very nice. The room was serviced twice a day, and a complimentary beverage was delivered in the morning - with our choice of beverages and delivery time. There were two computers in a small room at the hotel lobby for guests to use the Internet though the guest rooms also have free high-speed Internet. Overall, I had better experience at the Omni than I had in other 5 or 4-star hotels Ie stayed in SF, thanks to its personalized service. All the good things you read from the reviews are true.Besides service, another reason we picked the Omni is its location. It is in the middle of everything and right on the cable car line. It is two blocks from Chinatown ?very convenient for getting fresh Chinese pastries in the mornings. A few advices if you decide to stay at the Omni: (1) Sign up for the Select Guest program before you make the reservation. You can read the benefits on omnihotels.com. (2) Take public transportation (BART/MUNI) instead of renting a car. If you have to rent a car, rent it in the city and try to return on the same day, since overnight parking can be pricy. I like the MUNI Passport (for 1, 3 or 7 days), it is convenient if you ride cable cars a lot (we had to do that to make our 3-yr-old happy). (3) The hotel is big on great guest services, not on impressive architecture (like the Atrium of the Hyatt Regency) or in-house amenities/activities (such as a swimming pool) which is not a problem since it is close to many attractions anyway. Want be treated well on your next SF trip? Try the Omni San Francisco.

<Author>zuberry
<Content>Loved our stay at the Omni My husband and I plus 12 year old daughter stayed for three nights at the Omni and had a lovely stay. The hotel is entrance is extremely impressive with lovely marble floors and lots of wood etc. The staff were very welcoming and extremely helpful with all our requests - Joey on the front desk was particuarly charming and remembered my name with no problem at all. Our room was extremely comfortable, at the end of a corridor with a welcoming note and fresh fruit and chocs left each night. Location is not bad either. Just over a block to walk into China town, Union Square 20 mins or so, and a good walk to Fisherman's Wharf - about 25 mins (this was no problem as we enjoy walking when we have the time!) Cable car does stop outside but we did not really try to catch as preferred to walk each day. Having tried to stay at the Argonaut down at Fisherman Wharf (fully booked and on seeing the hotel during our visit) I am really glad we chose to stay at the Omni. The hotel is extremely comfortable and offers a quiet and distinctly elegant stay. Whilst in San Fran we had an excellent meal in China Town at the Empress of China (recommended by the front desk) and also at the Stinking Rose (Garlic Restuarant) which I think was in Little Italy. Also breakfast at Mamas was well worth the queue outside. One tip is if you want to go to Alcratraz book on line prior to arriving in San Fran as this was totally booked up when we arrived which meant we could not go on the trip. Also had a fabulous tour with Mr Toad's tours in a 1920's wooden open bus and the trip over by Ferry to Solsalido was fab.

<Author>neversummer
<Content>great location + Great rooms... I was planning a 2 night stay in SF, and using tripadvisor...Omni turned out to be the best bang for the buck. So, i want to return the favor and put in my 2 cents since i was able to save a lot of $$$. First off, if you want to do a weekend getaway... I would suggest Sat, Sun and check out Mon..instead of Fri-Sun... the biggest money drain is the parking...$45/night...if you park at St. Mary's parking...it is $30/nite..M-F...but only $6.50 during weekends! So...by going on Sat, Sun..you save quite a bit.Ok..the good: Very nice, clean, and classy hotel...service and attitude were top notch...doormen were friendly and eager to help... ladies on the desk were knowledgable and efficient. The room is average size, but the bathroom was very classy. No motel quality here...the shower is tiled natural stone...(marble or granite)...sink was nice granite, and huge framed vanity mirror...fancy shower curtains and nice tiled floor. I hate cheap crappy plastic bathrooms...The bed was a double queen...it was pretty good as well...ive slept in better beds but this will do. Overall the room was very clean and well appointed.Signing up for the Omni select guest is worth it...you should do it well in advance so you get the additional coupons for upgrades and discounts. You must do this in advance to activate them...Location wise...it is very ideal...next to chinatown 2 blocks, 4 blocks to Union square and 4 blocks to Embarcadero center and 3 blocks to columbus ave bars.. china town is up the hill but if you can make it to st. mary's parking lot...you can make it to chinatown. Honestly though, I think getting a hotel by fishermans wharf wouldve been a better location...but then, you'd get a Motel quality place for a Hotel price tag... i chose the hotel...If you have a baby or kids... fisherman's wharf would be a better fit. But if you like bars..i think Omni would be great since Columbus ave bars is just next door...very cool place. Awesome chinese food (dimsum also) at Harbor village in the embarcadero. (order the nobleman's chicken $80..a day in advance. Its called Beggar's chicken in Hong Kong...absolutely amazing) RG lounge is also good chinese food that's walking distance... peking duck is good...but Harbor village takes all the awards. If you like steaks...and not afraid to drop $50+...Bob's chop house is awesome. I loooove steak... breakfasts/lunch is more reasonable.... but they have all the best cuts at night. Defintely worth going to.The BAD.. No swimming pool or spa... after walking up hills and blocks of concrete pavement... you'd want a spa to relax in. None. Bummer for kids. Hotel was sold out...so my select guest coupons and discounts were useless for upgrades...so call in advance. Parking is highway robbery.. they should have discounts for guests.. Overall... it is still a good experience. its no resort...its a business hotel, and maybe not a good pick if you have kids...but if you want a good place to sleep with your wife or girlfriend...close by to bars and great food. And without all the other complaints of moldy bathrooms, smelly beds, and crappy A/C... a nice respectable hotel like this is worth it.

<Author>melodyMD
<Content>Great hotel in San Francisco Having stayed at many disappointing four star rated spots in SanFran, this hotel was very lovely. Although they did not have the double bed rooms we requested numerous times before arrival, they provided us with comfortable rollaways, and attempted to immediately move us to double bed rooms on the second night. Everything in the hotel functioned well- super clean rooms, great service, great location - its perfectly situated - between the busy busy union square area, and access to street cars for the wharf, or going to the North End Italian district on foot. Its very quiet at night and also right next to Chinatown. Altogether a great hotel with a great staff. My only complaint is the dinky free business center they have on the ground floor, where two free computers are provided for hotel guests use (because the room web-TV is hopelessly slow and disconnects). These computers have people sitting at them 24/7, with a line of guests waiting outside the door. You can keep checking back ten times and not make it onto the computers. While it is a nice courtesy to have these, I found the set up horrible and disruptive to the immediate lobby area. What they need to do is provide guests with a log in code each day, once a day, or a set period of use, say 15 minutes. That way people can't hog the computers for hours. Even worse, when trying to remedy this situation and offer additional computers behind the front desk to guests that have waited too long - there seems to be miscommunication between the hotel staff - with one happily offering extra computers for guests to use briefly, and another (the only nasty staff member we encountered at this hotel) rudely kicking us off shortly thereafter. Perhaps they'd be better off removing their courtesy computers. This is the only flaw in the hotel, and not much of one considering all the great service and amenities. I'd definitely stay here again, but I would bring my laptop.
